FILE: 0_Welcome_Lesson_DOC_0.txt

﻿RMBC II: Course Outline
Part 1. Foundations (What we Just Went Over Above)
* What is Copywriting? 
* The Two Crucial Customer Journeys You Need to Understand
* What Sales Funnels Look Like in 2025
* The True Purpose of Direct Response Marketing
* Context is King: Why All Advertising Starts With Product/Market Awareness and Platform-Specific Strategies.
* The RMBC II Approach: Simplifying Complexity & Leveraging AI.
Part 2. Deep Research
* Product/Market Awareness - What it Is, Why it Matters, the Deep Research Process for identifying the Product/Market Awareness Level of Your Core Customer (And How to Speak To Them). 
* Competitor Research - Deep Research Process for Doing Competitor Analysis to get Claims For Your Own Product and Differentiate Yourself From Competitors 
* Psychographic Research - Understanding the Deep Psychological Drivers of Your Prospect 
* Unified Research Document - Putting the Above Together Into One Document that Can be Fed to LLMs When Writing Copy 
* Ingredient Research (When Relevant) - Using Perplexity (Or Other LLMs) To Get Studies, Claims, and Citations for Any Supplement Formulation in Under 5 Minutes

Part 3. Unique Mechanisms 
* Overview
* UM Ideation With LLMs 
* UM Evaluation Process Using LLMs
* UM Expansion with Claude 
* Claude Project Setup for Unique Mechanisms

Part 4. VSL Copy Part I: Understanding Structures, Elements, Etc.
* Sales Copy Structure Core Training With Multiple Long and Medium For Examples
* Financial Long Form Example
* Medium Form VSL Breakdowns
* Short Form VSL Breakdowns
* Hooks Training
* ADHD Hook Video Ads
* In-Feed vs. On Page VSLs

Part 5. Brief 2.0
* The old brief vs the New Brief
* The Brief 2.0 Generator (Claude Project)
* Brief Generation Examples

Part 6. VSL Copy Part II 
* Setting Up Claude Project Recipes for Long, Medium, 3-7 Minute, and Short VSLs. 
* VSL Creation Walkthroughs and Examples:
Long, Medium, 3-7 Minutes, and Short

Part 7. RMBC II Mid-Course Recap
Summarizing everything we’ve covered so far, including an explicit breakdown of the processes you just learned and how they fit together. 

Part 8. Advertorials
* Overview of Advertorials Including Purposes, Common Elements, Why they Vary in Length, and How They Fit Into the Broader Marketing Funnel Context
* Specific Journey Walkthroughs: Meta and Native 
* Claude Projects Setup for Generating Endless Advertorials of All Lengths and for All Platforms

Part 9. PDPs (Landing Pages)
* PDP Overview: Different types, different lengths, and different purposes. Understanding why some are essentially long sales letters, and some are very short and basic. Fitting them into the overall A->B marketing funnel journey. 
* Numerous Breakdowns and Examples - deconstructing their purpose, important elements, etc. 
* Using AI to Create Outlines from Winning PDP Structures and then Instantly Generate New Ones

Part 10. Checkouts
* Walkthrough of Multiple Checkout Examples. Identifying common conversion elements and opportunities for improvement. Understanding why some are very basic and some are longer. 

Part 11. Ads
* In-Depth Walkthroughs of Various Ad Styles and Structures on Meta (SPG), Native (Dynh at Adxp), Google (David OConnell), TikTok (Maxwell Finn), and YouTube (Tom Clayson at Tried and True).
* AI Processes for Generating Winning Ad Copy Fast. 

Part 12. The 15 Factors that Determine Your Funnel Structure
* Gives you a specific set of criteria for evaluating any product or offer you’ll be selling, and then determining the optimal funnel structure to create. 
* This is insanely powerful and nobody has ever done a training like this to my knowledge. 

Section II: From B to C (and D, and E, and F, and ……)

Part 13. Upsells
* Psychology, Strategy, Funnel Economics, and Purposes of Upsells and Cross-Sells
* Multiple Upsell Walkthroughs including a Cleaning Product, Protein Bars, Supplements, Biz Opp, and Info Products
* Claude Project Setup and Examples for Generating Endless Upsells for Any Offer

Part 14. Email Marketing Journeys
* Abandon Carts - Purposes, Economics, and Why people Don’t Buy. Example Flows for Supplements and Book a Call Funnels.
* Welcome Series - Purpose, Walkthroughs for eCom Supplement, High Ticket (Consumption), and Digital Course with Push to Book a Coaching Call
* Promotional Sequences - Holiday Promos and Flash Sales with Examples for Supplements, Digital Product (BizOpp Saas). Includes 3 Day Sale, 5 Day Sale (Thanksgiving and Black Friday) and 24 Hour Flash Sale Examples for Both.
* Reorder Sequences and Winbacks. Reorder sequences for supplement buyers, Winback Sequences for Supplement Buyers and SaaS Subscription Cancelers. 
* Claude Project Setup and Walkthroughs for Generating Endless Email Sequences of Any Type and for Any Product or Service. 

Part 15. Bonuses
* CRO Best Practices and Case Studies with 4080 Marketing
* eCom and Amazon with Eddie Maalouf
* Funnel Economics with Stefan
* High Ticket Webinar Structure and Copy with Dylan Vanas
* The State of VSLs in 2025: Benchmarks and Insider Data with Patrick Stiles - Founder of Vidalytics

﻿Reminder: Use this Prompt in the Unique Mechanism Claude Project (See Separate Training For How to Set This Project Up)

Example 1:

We’re going to do an in-depth unique mechanism for a product. I’ve attached a unified research document that should give you a strong overview of the target market. 

Here is a summary of the UMP and UMS:

Mechanism 2.1: The "Asset Gap" vs. The "Income Gap"
* The Unique Mechanism of the Problem (UMP): You have been trying to solve an Asset Gap problem with an Income Gap solution. The prospect correctly identifies the symptom: the squeeze of stagnant wages against the rising cost of living. Their logical, yet flawed, conclusion is that they simply need to "make more money." This leads them down the path of side hustles, which are fundamentally  
* Income Gap solutions. These hustles may provide a temporary, marginal increase in monthly earnings, but they do nothing to address the core, underlying disease. The "rigged game" is not merely about the size of one's paycheck; it is about the structural divide between those who build wealth through appreciating, cash-flowing assets and those who are confined to earning active income. Their past failures in dropshipping, freelancing, and gig work were preordained because these activities never allowed them to cross the chasm from the world of labor to the world of assets. They were merely patching a leaking boat instead of building a new one.
* The Unique Mechanism of the Solution (UMS): The program teaches the "Asset Control" method, the first system that allows you to leapfrog the "Income Gap" and directly address the "Asset Gap." Rental arbitrage, through this lens, is presented as a paradigm shift. It is the first viable strategy for the capital-constrained individual to gain control over a high-value, cash-flowing asset—a residential property—without needing the hundreds of thousands of dollars in capital or the pristine credit required for traditional ownership. By leasing a property long-term and operating it as a short-term rental, the prospect fundamentally alters their position in the economic hierarchy. They stop being a seller of their own time and become an operator of an asset. This mechanism transforms the program from a "how-to" guide into a strategic blueprint for changing one's fundamental economic identity. It directly delivers on the promise of "building wealth through real estate without the need for mortgages or large down payments".  

===
For this exercise, let's specifically focus on people in the market who are Problem Aware.
Please go ahead and write the Unique Mechanism section in a format that could be used in a video sales letter. 

======================
Example 2:

We’re going to do an in-depth unique mechanism for a product. I’ve attached a unified research document that should give you a strong overview of the target market. 

Here is a summary of the UMP and UMS:

Unique Mechanism: The "Permission-Based" Income Trap
The Problem Mechanism
A unifying thread running through every source of frustration in the prospect's financial life is that all their income is Permission-Based. Their ability to earn money is perpetually at the mercy of a third party, which explains their profound "lack of control over their time, schedule, and life decisions".  
This framework can be used to diagnose all their past and present struggles:
   * The 9-to-5 Job: Their primary income is based on their boss's permission to remain employed.
   * Gig Economy Work: Income from platforms like Uber or DoorDash is based on the permission of an algorithm that can change their earning potential without notice.
   * Freelancing: Income is contingent on a client's permission to continue the contract.
   * Online Businesses: Their dropshipping or affiliate marketing income was fundamentally based on the permission of ad platforms like Facebook and Google, which are notorious for shutting down accounts overnight, instantly vaporizing a business.
This "Permission-Based" framework gives a single, damning label to all their experiences of powerlessness. It shows them that whether they were working for a boss or for themselves, they were never truly in control. They were always asking for permission to earn a living.
The Solution Mechanism: The "Permissionless Cashflow System"
The program teaches them how to build a Permissionless Cashflow System. This mechanism directly counters the trap of permission-based income by creating a business where, after an initial setup phase, the income stream is generated by the open market and flows directly to them.
The process involves a single, critical point of permission: negotiating the lease and arbitrage addendum with a property owner. This is framed not as asking for permission in the same vein as a boss or an algorithm, but as a strategic, one-time partnership negotiation to acquire a "master key" to an asset.
Once this "master key" is secured and the property is listed, the dynamic shifts entirely:
   * No boss can fire them from their property.
   * No algorithm can suddenly deprioritize their listing and slash their income.
   * No client can decide to stop paying them.
   * The income is generated by travelers and guests in the free market, and the cash flow is deposited directly into their account.
This mechanism powerfully delivers on the core promises of "take back control" and "be your own boss". It positions the business not as another fragile venture dependent on the whims of others, but as a robust, resilient system for generating income on their own terms. It offers a tangible path to the autonomy they crave more than anything else.  

===
For this exercise, let's specifically focus on people in the market who are Problem Aware.
Please go ahead and write the Unique Mechanism section in a format that could be used in a video sales letter. 

======================
Example 3:

We’re going to do an in-depth unique mechanism for a product. I’ve attached a unified research document that should give you a strong overview of the target market. 

Here is a summary of the UMP and UMS:

The Problem (UMP) - The Lipid Barrier Breach & "Inflamm-Aging"
This mechanism focuses on the skin's most fundamental point of failure: its first line of defense. The problem is a Lipid Barrier Breach. The skin's protective outer layer, the stratum corneum, can be visualized as a "brick and mortar" wall. The skin cells (corneocytes) are the bricks, and the lipids (fats) surrounding them are the mortar. With age, hormonal changes, and environmental stress, this lipid mortar begins to degrade, developing microscopic cracks and gaps.
This breach has two devastating consequences that directly map to the consumer's frustrations:
   1. Uncontrolled Moisture Loss: The cracks in the barrier act like an open window, allowing the skin's precious moisture to escape unchecked. This leads to the chronic dryness, tightness, and flakiness she experiences.
   2. The Gateway to "Inflamm-Aging": More insidiously, the breach creates an open door for external irritants, pollutants, and allergens to penetrate deep into the skin. This constant influx of foreign invaders triggers the immune system, creating a state of persistent, low-grade inflammation. Scientists have given this phenomenon a name: "Inflamm-Aging". It is a chronic, silent inflammatory state that constantly stimulates the production of collagen- and elastin-degrading enzymes, silently accelerating all visible signs of aging.  
This mechanism perfectly explains her practical frustration with "product sensitivity" and experiencing "reactions, burning, irritation from potent ingredients". Her skin's protective wall is compromised, so even well-formulated active ingredients can feel harsh and cause a reaction because they are penetrating too quickly and deeply into an already inflamed environment.  
The Solution (UMS) - The "Biomimetic Barrier Seal"
The only way to address the consequences of a breached barrier is to repair the wall itself. The solution is a "Biomimetic Barrier Seal," a complex of intelligent emollients that patch the cracks and restore the barrier's integrity.
1. The Sealants (Cupuacu Butter & Jojoba Esters): The serum utilizes two key ingredients for this task: Cupuacu Seed Butter and Jojoba Esters. These are not just simple moisturizers; they are chosen for their biomimetic properties, meaning their lipid structures are remarkably similar to the natural fats and oils found in healthy skin, allowing them to integrate seamlessly.  
   * Cupuacu Seed Butter: This Amazonian "super-moisturizer" is prized for its rich content of phytosterols and essential fatty acids, which are the exact components needed to replenish the lipid "mortar". It possesses an unparalleled ability to attract and hold water—up to 440% of its own weight—which allows it to function as a powerful hydrator, drawing moisture back into the skin and holding it there.  
   * Jojoba Esters: Derived from Jojoba oil, these esters have a molecular structure that closely mimics human sebum. This allows them to blend into the skin's natural barrier, locking in moisture and providing a soft, non-greasy feel while reinforcing the wall's structure.  
2. Ending "Inflamm-Aging": Together, these ingredients act like a flexible, breathable spackle, filling the cracks in the lipid barrier. This action immediately accomplishes two critical goals. First, it stops transepidermal water loss, alleviating dryness and restoring suppleness. Second, and more importantly, it closes the door to external irritants, blocking the primary trigger for "Inflamm-Aging." By sealing the breach, the "Biomimetic Barrier Seal" extinguishes the inflammatory fire, calming the skin and creating a protected, stable environment. This not only makes the skin feel more comfortable but also allows the other powerful peptides and vitamins in the serum to perform their repair work effectively and without causing irritation, directly addressing her fear of sensitivity and delivering on the promise of a product that is both powerful and gentle.  

===
For this exercise, let's specifically focus on people in the market who are Solution Aware.

Here’s how you can understand Solution Aware in this context:

The Solution Aware (Estimated 40-45% of TAM)

Profile: Representing the largest segment of the market, the Solution Aware consumer has made a significant leap. She knows her problem (e.g., wrinkles, dark circles) and now knows that a category of products—generically referred to as "eye cream" or "eye serum"—exists to address it. Her primary goal is to find the "best" one for her specific issue. However, at this stage, her understanding is typically not rooted in ingredient science. She evaluates products based on brand reputation, price, packaging, key benefit claims (e.g., "brightening," "firming," "hydrating"), and, most importantly, social proof in the form of reviews and recommendations.

Please go ahead and write the Unique Mechanism section in a format that could be used in a video sales letter.

Example 4:

We’re going to do an in-depth unique mechanism for a product. I’ve attached a unified research document that should give you a strong overview of the target market. 

Here is a summary of the UMP and UMS:

The Problem (UMP) - Dermal Disarray: The Hidden Structural Chaos
For years, the prevailing narrative sold to this consumer has been one of simple "collagen loss." She has been told that her skin is wrinkling and losing firmness because this crucial protein is depleting with age. This explanation, however, is incomplete and fails to account for why the numerous "collagen-boosting" products she has tried have proven inadequate.  
The real, more insidious problem is not just loss, but disorganization. The underlying issue is a state of Dermal Disarray, where her existing collagen fibers have become tangled, weakened, and chaotic. Instead of a strong, tightly woven mesh providing firm support, her dermal structure has devolved into a disorganized tangle. This structural chaos is what allows the skin to fold into permanent wrinkles and lose its youthful tautness.
This can be visualized using the analogy of a tent. Her previous solutions were like trying to patch small holes in the tent's fabric (addressing collagen loss). But the real problem is that the tent poles have collapsed and become jumbled (Dermal Disarray). No matter how perfectly the fabric is patched, the tent has no structure and cannot stand firm. The feeling of skin losing its "snap" and lines becoming permanently etched is far better described by this kind of catastrophic structural failure than by simple depletion. By defining the problem as Dermal Disarray, we create a new knowledge gap and position our solution as uniquely equipped to address this previously undiagnosed issue.
The Solution (UMS) - The "Bio-Tensegrity" Signal & Smart Materials
The solution to Dermal Disarray is not to crudely attempt to pump more material into a collapsed structure, but to restore its architectural integrity. This is achieved through a two-part system that re-establishes order and provides the precise materials for reconstruction.
1. The "Bio-Tensegrity" Signal (Dipalmitoyl Hydroxyproline): The primary hero ingredient, Dipalmitoyl Hydroxyproline (DPHP), is introduced not as a generic peptide but as a "Bio-Tensegrity" signaling molecule. Its specific function is to command the skin's own machinery to correct the chaos. It works by stimulating the contraction of existing collagen fibers, effectively pulling the tangled network taut and restoring its organized, strong, and resilient structure. This process actively "firms the tissues" and helps "optimize the arrangement of collagen fibers". To ensure this critical signal reaches its target, DPHP is chemically modified with palmitic acid, a fatty acid that increases its lipophilicity, allowing it to penetrate the skin's lipid layers and work deep within the dermis where the disarray exists.  
2. The "Smart Materials" (Amino Acids): Once the command to rebuild has been issued, the skin needs the right building blocks on-site. The formula provides these in the form of the amino acids Proline, Glycine, and Alanine. These are not a random assortment of proteins; they are the specific, pre-sorted "smart materials" required for collagen synthesis. Glycine is found at almost every third residue in the collagen sequence, while Proline makes up about 17% of collagen. By delivering these key components topically, the serum gives the skin the exact raw materials it needs to efficiently execute the "Bio-Tensegrity" signal and rebuild its framework.  
3. The Protective Shield (Dipalmitoyl Hydroxyproline): Finally, to ensure the newly restored structure is protected, DPHP also acts as a guardian. It inhibits the function of matrix metalloproteinases (MMPs), the very enzymes that degrade collagen and contribute to disarray. It also protects the skin's elastin fibers from enzymatic lysis. This defensive action ensures that the restored dermal architecture is shielded from the forces that caused its collapse in the first place, leading to lasting, visible improvement in firmness and smoothness.  

===
For this exercise, let's specifically focus on people in the market who are Solution Aware.

Here’s how you can understand Solution Aware in this context:

The Solution Aware (Estimated 40-45% of TAM)

Profile: Representing the largest segment of the market, the Solution Aware consumer has made a significant leap. She knows her problem (e.g., wrinkles, dark circles) and now knows that a category of products—generically referred to as "eye cream" or "eye serum"—exists to address it. Her primary goal is to find the "best" one for her specific issue. However, at this stage, her understanding is typically not rooted in ingredient science. She evaluates products based on brand reputation, price, packaging, key benefit claims (e.g., "brightening," "firming," "hydrating"), and, most importantly, social proof in the form of reviews and recommendations.

Please go ahead and write the Unique Mechanism section in a format that could be used in a video sales letter.

﻿Very Simple Sales Letter Outline:
* Hook/Microlead
* Lead
* Background (Credibility and Origin Story)
* Discovery
* UMP/UMS
* Product Build-Up and Reveal
* Close
* FAQ

Example Formats: 
6 Minute VSL
Will return to this.

15 Minute VSL
Eg 1: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1BAESwq17ji50IuO7Wq0-snyp-yZHI4rKZwSSTBD8dEA/edit?usp=sharing

Eg2: 
https://docs.google.com/document/d/1eYZkzKYmez-SAmAmlipHv69n2xkeWIdZcqISfoEug4c/edit?usp=sharing

35 Minute VSL:
https://youtu.be/ewH5uZVjaAY?si=39SX6xu_set5RG56

Sales Letter Outline: 

* Support points - you don't necessarily have to use everything
** The order within a point is not necessarily in that order - they can also “mix” with each other

1. Pre-Lead/MicroLead
1. -Hook heavy or attention grabbing opening line. 
2. - Quickly related to the pain-point prospect faces 
3. - Quick related to the promise of a solution 

Nooro Ads Library:
https://www.facebook.com/ads/library/?active_status=all&ad_type=all&country=US&view_all_page_id=107580105023479&search_type=page&media_type=all

Nooro Similar Web:
https://pro.similarweb.com/?#/digitalsuite/websiteanalysis/referrals/incoming-traffic/*/999/3m?webSource=Total&key=nooro-us.com

2. Lead (These Don’t Have to be in order) (Open a bunch of loops with fascinations, and say - I’m going to get to that in just a moment, or a few minutes, or “and you’ll see that in this video”
   1. Call Out Problem 
   2. Promise Solution to Pain Point + Promise to Save Time/Money 
   3. Tease Emotional Discovery Story 
   4. Tease Unique Mechanism Behind Solution 
   5. Tease Contrarian Nature of Mechanism (This Flies in the Face of What You’ve Been Told Before)
   6. Working in “Fascinations” as Incentive For Continuing With Copy (I’ll Answer This Riddle For You)
   7. Briefly Mention Credibility Builders
   8. Qualifiers – Who This Works For. Is It For Everyone? Is It For a Certain Subset? Speak to Your Market. 
   9. Briefly Address Skepticism.  
   10. Include a Few Broad Testimonials if Available (About Benefits But Don’t Give Away Product)

3. II. Background Story
   1. Who I Am + Credibility Builders When Appropriate (ie. A Doctor or Expert) 
   2. “Me or Someone Close to Me Was Just Like You (In Pain)” – Here’s The Emotional Story About It
   3. Traditional Solutions & Advice Not Working
   4. Trigger Event – Problem or Pain Point Escalated to Where Avatar Realizes Something MUST Change
   5. Search for Truth/Answers 

   4. III. Unique Mechanism of the Problem

      1. Explaining the “Real Cause” of the Problem; You’ve Had 99% of the Answer But This is the Missing 1%  
      2. Should Be Surprising, Possibly Even Counterintuitive 
      3. Backed by Credibility and Proof Elements 

         5. Unique Mechanism of The Solution
         1. Now That You Know the Real Cause of the Problem, This is the “Real Solution” on a MACRO level. 
         2. This Should Be Logically Connected to the Problem 
         3. Once They Have the MACRO Solution (A Theory) – They Dig Deep To Prove The Theory (And Get Into The MICRO). 
         4. Backed By Credibility and Proof Elements, Including Citations and Scientific Sources.

            6.  V. Product Buildup + Reveal

               1. Now That Avatar Knows The Solution, He Looks For An “Out-of-the-Box” Version; Something That Will Just End His Quest and Solve The Problem Right There
               2. But Discovers That Out-of-the-Box Is Flawed 
               3. Has to Do It Himself And Create Novel New Solution
               4. Starts Testing It or Working On It. There Are Problems and Setbacks
               5. But Eventual Success/Breakthrough
               6. Proof Product Works
               7. Others Asking For It
               8. PRODUCT Is Born!

               7. VI. Close 

                  1. Product Details (What’s Included, What Makes it Special, Unique Selling Propositions)
                  2. Discuss and Dismiss Other Alternatives (Expensive, Ineffective, Side-Effects, Poor Quality, Unproven)
                  3. Keep Building Up Value of -PRODUCT-
                  4. Additional Testimonials
                  5. How to Use The Product
                  6. Scarcity: Demand Is High, Supplies Are Limited, Out-of-Stocks Are Common
                  7. Personal Mission of Avatar to Make Things Better – Tied to Emotion
                  8. Price Justification & Reveal – Other “Solutions” Are More Expensive & Consequences of Inaction are Costly (Cost Can Be Either Material or Immaterial)
                  9. This Solution is Better and Will Save You Money, It’s Normally $X Which is Bargain, But Right Now You Can Get It For Just $Y!
                  10. Smart People Buy More

                  8. First Call to Action 
                  1. What Happens After You Click The Button
                  2. Optional: Valuable Free Bonuses Revealed
                  3. Guarantee – You’ll Most Likely Have a Great Experience, But If For Any Reason You Don’t, No Risk and No Hassle

                  9. Second Call to Action 
                  1. Two Choices – You Can Go On Suffering, Or You Can Take Action Today and Change Your Life forever; The Choice Is Yours
                  2. Urgency 2 – But You Really Must Hurry As This is The End of the Presentation And There’s No Guarantee How Long Offer Will Be Available

                  10. Third Call to Action 
                  1. Thank You For Watching

                  11. VII. FAQs
                  1. Back to Being Their Friend; Helping To Clear Up Any Confusion They May Have
                  2. Reminding Them of What Product Is, What It’s Used For, Importance of Taking Action Today, Terms of Guarantee, and How to Buy!

﻿Very Simple Sales Letter Outline:
* Hook/Microlead
* Lead
* Background (Credibility and Origin Story)
* Discovery
* UMP/UMS
* Product Build-Up and Reveal
* Close
* FAQ

Sales Letter Outline: 

* Support points - you don't necessarily have to use everything
** The order within a point is not necessarily in that order - they can also “mix” with each other

1. Pre-Lead/MicroLead
1. -Hook heavy or attention grabbing opening line. 
2. - Quickly related to the pain-point prospect faces 
3. - Quick related to the promise of a solution 

2. Lead (These Don’t Have to be in order) (Open a bunch of loops with fascinations, and say - I’m going to get to that in just a moment, or a few minutes, or “and you’ll see that in this video”
   1. Call Out Problem 
   2. Promise Solution to Pain Point + Promise to Save Time/Money 
   3. Tease Emotional Discovery Story 
   4. Tease Unique Mechanism Behind Solution 
   5. Tease Contrarian Nature of Mechanism (This Flies in the Face of What You’ve Been Told Before)
   6. Working in “Fascinations” as Incentive For Continuing With Copy (I’ll Answer This Riddle For You)
   7. Briefly Mention Credibility Builders
   8. Qualifiers – Who This Works For. Is It For Everyone? Is It For a Certain Subset? Speak to Your Market. 
   9. Briefly Address Skepticism.  
   10. Include a Few Broad Testimonials if Available (About Benefits But Don’t Give Away Product)

3. II. Background Story
   1. Who I Am + Credibility Builders When Appropriate (ie. A Doctor or Expert) 
   2. “Me or Someone Close to Me Was Just Like You (In Pain)” – Here’s The Emotional Story About It
   3. Traditional Solutions & Advice Not Working
   4. Trigger Event – Problem or Pain Point Escalated to Where Avatar Realizes Something MUST Change
   5. Search for Truth/Answers 

   4. III. Unique Mechanism of the Problem

      1. Explaining the “Real Cause” of the Problem; You’ve Had 99% of the Answer But This is the Missing 1%  
      2. Should Be Surprising, Possibly Even Counterintuitive 
      3. Backed by Credibility and Proof Elements 

         5. Unique Mechanism of The Solution
         1. Now That You Know the Real Cause of the Problem, This is the “Real Solution” on a MACRO level. 
         2. This Should Be Logically Connected to the Problem 
         3. Once They Have the MACRO Solution (A Theory) – They Dig Deep To Prove The Theory (And Get Into The MICRO). 
         4. Backed By Credibility and Proof Elements, Including Citations and Scientific Sources.

            6.  V. Product Buildup + Reveal

               1. Now That Avatar Knows The Solution, He Looks For An “Out-of-the-Box” Version; Something That Will Just End His Quest and Solve The Problem Right There
               2. But Discovers That Out-of-the-Box Is Flawed 
               3. Has to Do It Himself And Create Novel New Solution
               4. Starts Testing It or Working On It. There Are Problems and Setbacks
               5. But Eventual Success/Breakthrough
               6. Proof Product Works
               7. Others Asking For It
               8. PRODUCT Is Born!

               7. VI. Close 

                  1. Product Details (What’s Included, What Makes it Special, Unique Selling Propositions)
                  2. Discuss and Dismiss Other Alternatives (Expensive, Ineffective, Side-Effects, Poor Quality, Unproven)
                  3. Keep Building Up Value of -PRODUCT-
                  4. Additional Testimonials
                  5. How to Use The Product
                  6. Scarcity: Demand Is High, Supplies Are Limited, Out-of-Stocks Are Common
                  7. Personal Mission of Avatar to Make Things Better – Tied to Emotion
                  8. Price Justification & Reveal – Other “Solutions” Are More Expensive & Consequences of Inaction are Costly (Cost Can Be Either Material or Immaterial)
                  9. This Solution is Better and Will Save You Money, It’s Normally $X Which is Bargain, But Right Now You Can Get It For Just $Y!
                  10. Smart People Buy More

                  8. First Call to Action 
                  1. What Happens After You Click The Button
                  2. Optional: Valuable Free Bonuses Revealed
                  3. Guarantee – You’ll Most Likely Have a Great Experience, But If For Any Reason You Don’t, No Risk and No Hassle

                  9. Second Call to Action 
                  1. Two Choices – You Can Go On Suffering, Or You Can Take Action Today and Change Your Life forever; The Choice Is Yours
                  2. Urgency 2 – But You Really Must Hurry As This is The End of the Presentation And There’s No Guarantee How Long Offer Will Be Available

                  10. Third Call to Action 
                  1. Thank You For Watching

                  11. VII. FAQs
                  1. Back to Being Their Friend; Helping To Clear Up Any Confusion They May Have
                  2. Reminding Them of What Product Is, What It’s Used For, Importance of Taking Action Today, Terms of Guarantee, and How to Buy!

================================================================================
FILE: 1_DTC_Marketing_2025_Lesson_DOC_2.txt
================================================================================

﻿Part I. Copywriting and the State of Direct Response in 2025
In this opening section we’ll be covering:
* What is Copywriting? 
* The Two Crucial Customer Journeys You Need to Understand
* What Sales Funnels Look Like in 2025
* The True Purpose of Direct Response Marketing
* Why Context is King: Why All Advertising Starts With Product/Market Awareness and Platform-Specific Strategies.
* The RMBC II Approach: Simplifying Complexity & Leveraging AI.
Let's start at the beginning: What is Copywriting?
On a fundamental level, it’s the art and science of writing advertisements. Simple, right?
We’ll dive much deeper into this, of course. But one of the most effective ways to conceptualize copywriting is by thinking about it in the context of two critical customer journeys:
Journey #1: From Prospect to Purchaser 
This is where someone starts at Point A (not a customer) and, through your efforts, arrives at Point B (they become a paying customer).
Journey #2: From Customer to Repeat Champion 
Here, someone who is already at Point B (a customer) embarks on a new path to Point C (becoming a loyal, repeat customer).
We'll explore Journey #2 in detail later in this course. 
For now, our primary focus will be on mastering Journey #1: Guiding someone from Point A (not a customer) to Point B (a customer).
This first journey is often visualized as a “sales funnel.”
  

So, how does an individual begin this journey? They might encounter a business through:
1. An Advertisement: This is our main playground in RMBC II.
2. Organic Discovery: Think stumbling upon a brand or product via a Google search, Browse Amazon, walking past a physical store, or even asking someone where they got a product.
3. A Recommendation: Word-of-mouth from a friend, an influencer mention, or a review.
While all are important, RMBC II will concentrate primarily on creating powerful advertisements.
Alright, so a potential customer sees an ad. Where does this happen? The digital landscape is vast:
* Facebook
* Instagram
* Native Ad Networks (e.g., Taboola, Outbrain)
* TikTok
* YouTube
* Google Display Network
* Google Search (PPC)
* In-App Advertising (e.g., AppLovin)
* Shopify App Ecosystem (e.g., ShopApp)
* Amazon (Sponsored Products, Brands, Display)
* Email Marketing
* And yes, even traditional platforms like Radio & TV (though our digital focus will be paramount).
These are all platforms where a prospective customer might encounter your "ad." Crucially, ads will typically look, feel, and be written differently depending on the platform. We're going to explore this in depth below.
But for now, let's say they see an ad.
If that ad is a good one*, it compels the person to take a specific action. In other words, the ad elicits a direct response.
And that, in essence, is Direct Response Copywriting: writing ads and other marketing materials designed to get a prospective customer to take an immediate, measurable action.
That action could be to:
* Call a number
* Click a link
* Buy a product
* Share a post
* Sign up for a newsletter
* And so on...
The key is that they are taking action.
The sole criterion by which we judge an ad's effectiveness—whether it's "good" or not—is its ability to get the right kind of people to consistently take that desired action when they see it.
So, let's assume we have a "good ad." A prospect sees it and responds by clicking. What happens next?
The ultra-simplified version looks like this: 
They click an ad ➡️ Go to a website ➡️ Add a product to their cart ➡️ Complete the checkout.
Easy-peasy, right?
Well… it can be that simple, but it rarely is.
The truth about Direct Response Copywriting, and Direct Response Marketing in general, is that context is extremely important.
To understand why, let's revisit those platforms: (Facebook, Instagram, Native, TikTok, YouTube, Google Display, Google Search, In-App, ShopApp, Amazon, Email, etc.)
I mentioned that ads look different depending on the platform. That's true. But there’s even more to it: a customer’s journey will also often be different depending on the platform.
Let's look at a couple of quick examples:
Platform-Specific Journey Example #1: YouTube
  

* Why is a person on YouTube? Typically, to watch videos – either for education or entertainment.
* What does this mean for your YouTube Ads?
   * Firstly, your ads on YouTube will usually be video (there are exceptions and other types, but we’ll focus on video for now).
   * Secondly, ads that are more educational or entertaining often outperform those that aggressively hard-sell from the outset.
   * * Where should a customer go after clicking a YouTube Ad?
   * Often, to a page on your website that features… another video! This could be a long-form Video Sales Letter (VSL) or a shorter, more focused video. Why? Because they're already in a video-watching mindset.
   * Is this video always a VSL? Sometimes yes, sometimes no. We'll unpack VSLs in great detail soon.
Platform-Specific Journey Example #2: Native Advertising
  

* When does a person typically see a native ad? Usually when they're reading articles online – news, celebrity gossip, how-to guides, sports updates, or content related to any other interest (affinity).
* What does this mean for your Native Ads? A native ad is designed to look and read like it will link to an interesting news story or an intriguing article, blending in with the surrounding content.
* Where should a customer go after clicking a Native Ad? Typically, to an advertorial – an advertisement meticulously crafted to look and feel like an editorial piece or a news story. This maintains congruence in the customer journey.
Congruence: The act or goal of maintaining a consistent feeling experience for a prospect throughout their journey from Point A to Point B. 
Context Element #2: Product/Market Awareness.
This is actually one of the most important parts of RMBC II, but I’m not going to overexplain it here. I’ll just share some quick remarks, and we’ll dive into this a lot more afterwards. 

==============
Okay, let's return to our overarching customer journey. Remember, we're trying to get your prospect from Point A (Seeing an Ad) to Point B (Buying Your Product or Service).
So far, they have:
1. Seen the Ad
2. Clicked the Ad
3. Landed on a context-specific page on your website (e.g., a page with a video after a YouTube ad, or an advertorial after a native ad).
What happens next? It depends.
Let’s stick with our native example to illustrate: Native Ad ➡️ Advertorial ➡️ ???
Where do they go from the advertorial? This is where paths can diverge, and there isn't always one single "correct" answer.
For example:
* Scenario A: If the advertorial is quite long (say, 1,000 - 2,000+ words) and the product costs less than $50, the next step might be to go directly to a Product Page (PDP).

   * PDP Definition: A Product Detail Page (PDP) is a page on an e-commerce website that provides comprehensive information about a specific product. This includes images, descriptions, specifications, price, customer reviews, and the "add to cart" button.
   * Why this path? The long advertorial has presumably educated the prospect, built desire, and "sold" them on the value and need for your product. The lower price point means it’s an easier "impulse" purchase decision. The PDP then just needs to provide specific details, confirm it solves their pain points, and layer on social proof (testimonials, reviews, etc.). A good PDP excels at this.

   * Scenario B: Now, let's say the advertorial is much shorter (e.g., 200-400 words), and the product price is above $50.

      * In this case, the best place to send a prospective customer might be a landing page featuring a Video Sales Letter (VSL).
      * VSL = Essentially an online infomercial, a persuasive video presentation designed to sell a product or service.
We’ll dedicate significant time to VSLs in this course, but here are a few key highlights of what a VSL aims to do: 
      * Hook the prospect within the first 5 seconds, often using curiosity or a problem-solution framework. 
      * Build rapport and establish credibility. 
      * Share a compelling "hero's journey" story. 
      * Explain your Unique Mechanism of Product (UMP) and Unique Mechanism of Solution (UMS). 
      * Present the product as the ultimate way to experience the UMS. 
      * Build up a high perceived value for the product. 
      * Reveal the price or promise a big discount, making it seem like a fantastic deal in comparison to the value. 
      * Explicitly tell the prospect to buy the product with a clear Call to Action.
Important VSL Note: We're discussing VSLs on website landing pages in this example.They are also extremely popular and effective as ads themselves, especially on platforms like Meta (Facebook/Instagram). VSL length can vary wildly, from 2 minutes to over an hour.
Okay, Now Let's take a brief pause. 
So far, we've journeyed from understanding what copywriting is, to the initial customer journey, the role of ads, platform context, and how different ad types lead to different initial landing page experiences like advertorials or VSLs. You're already getting a glimpse of the strategic thinking involved, but we’ve also got further to go. 
So Let’s Continue Our Journey:
After a prospect has responded to an ad and engaged with advertorial/VSL/PDP…
We need them to take another action: selecting a product and adding it to their cart.
This typically brings them to the checkout page.
And guess what? Our work still isn't done.
On the checkout page, we need the prospect to take the biggest action of all. They need to:
      * Enter their personal information.
      * Enter their credit card details.
      * Mentally prepare to part with their money.
      * Make that final commitment by clicking "Place Order."
And here’s a fascinating detail: even the copy on a checkout page can vary significantly, from very short to surprisingly long. We’ll explore checkouts in much more detail later, but for now I want to help preserve your sanity. 
________________

Alright, the good news: at this point, we’ve conceptually completed the FIRST customer journey – getting them from Point A (not a paying customer) to Point B (a paying customer).
That's exciting!
However, one thought that should be crossing your mind right now (because as one of the best marketers in the world, it’s definitely crossing mine) is: "DAMN, Marketing Can Be HARD."
And you know what? It can be.
Especially when you consider all the individual components and how they can be combined in seemingly endless ways:
      * Ad Types: Static Ads (Native, Meta, Amazon, Instagram, ShopApp, Google), Short Video Ads (YouTube, Meta, TikTok), Medium Video Ads (YouTube, Meta), Long Video Ads (Meta).
      * Presell Pages: Short Advertorials (Native, Meta, AppLovin, TikTok, YouTube?), Medium Advertorials, Long Advertorials.
      * Sales Pages: Landing Page with Short VSL (Native, Meta, YouTube, AppLovin, TikTok), Medium VSL, Long VSL.
      * Product Pages: Short PDP, Medium PDP, Long PDP.
      * Checkout Flows: 1-Step, 2-Step; Short Checkout Copy, Medium Checkout Copy, Long Checkout Copy.
It feels like a LOT, right?
But it doesn’t have to be so overwhelming, and here’s why:
First, when you zoom out, we are really only orchestrating a few core funnel flows:
      1. Ad ➡️ VSL ➡️ Checkout
      2. Ad ➡️ Advertorial ➡️ VSL ➡️ Checkout
      3. Ad ➡️ Advertorial ➡️ VSL ➡️ PDP ➡️ Checkout
      4. Ad ➡️ PDP ➡️ Checkout
      5. Ad ➡️ Advertorial ➡️ PDP ➡️ Checkout
See? That’s already less overwhelming. Yes, the type of ad, advertorial, VSL, PDP, and checkout can all vary – but that’s okay. We’ll cover all those variations systematically throughout this course.

  

Second, you have a HUGE advantage as you embark on this journey: transparency into what already works.
What do I mean? The simplest way to write effective copy for a product is often to model what other successful brands selling similar products are already doing.
You don’t need to reinvent the wheel (and you rarely should). Just model what is proven to be working. This concept of "swiping" and adapting successful structures is a cornerstone of what you’ll learn in RMBC II. We’ll be dissecting effective copy across every stage of the sales funnel by looking at real-world examples, showing you what’s working and, crucially, equipping you with the knowledge and confidence to model these assets effectively.
And wait, it gets even better.
Thanks to the rise of Large Language Models (LLMs) and the specific processes you will learn inside RMBC II, it’s now easier than ever to write extremely good copy for all these funnel assets – in anywhere from just 5 minutes to perhaps a few hours at most.
This is a radical shift from when I launched the original RMBC Method in 2020. Back then, if I talked about writing a long-form VSL in a single week, people were astounded. When I mentioned the whole process took me about 12-16 hours, it sounded like I’d cracked the ultimate efficiency code.
Now? 12-16 hours for a VSL is dinosaur time.
I can comfortably write 2-4 high-quality VSLs in a single day, with each taking me about 2 hours, max. For you, starting out, it might take a bit longer – but definitely no more than 5 days for a great VSL, and likely much faster as your comfort and confidence grow.
And that’s just VSLs. The same acceleration applies to all other aspects of the copywriting process too. This is a huge part of RMBC II. 
You’ll discover how to leverage tools like Claude, OpenAI's ChatGPT, Perplexity, and other LLMs to:
      * Pump out 5-10 high-quality advertorials a day, easily.
      * Write 20-40 GOOD ads in a single day.
      * Generate 100+ promising angles/hooks at a time (for testing in ads, VSLs, emails, and more).
      * Create a compelling upsell (text or video script) in about an hour.
      * Draft a 7 or even 14-day email sequence in an hour too.
      * Conduct deep research to uncover unique mechanisms, ingredient benefits, and even "Big Ideas."
      * Produce 5-10 different winning Product Pages in a single afternoon.
It’s all proven, and it’s truly incredible. We're in a magical golden age where AI handles much of the heavy lifting, but your knowledge, strategic thinking, and confidence as a copywriting expert become the critical differentiating factors.
And that’s exactly what RMBC II is designed to give you.
      1. Deconstruct: We’re first going to dissect every single type of copy you’re likely to encounter, whether you're a freelance copywriter, an in-house marketer, an executive, or a business owner. You’ll understand the theory, the structure, and all the essential elements for each, so you can discern what makes a piece of copy great versus merely good, mediocre, or downright bad. And yes, there will be plenty of examples.
      2. Accelerate with AI: Then, you’ll be handed specific, AI-first processes. These show you exactly how to partner with AI, turning it into a world-class assistant that produces killer first drafts (often, these are close to final drafts!).
      3. Master the Craft: Finally, you’ll be shown how to “think and edit” like a top-tier copywriter, enabling you to apply those crucial refinements that transform B or A- copy into A+ masterpieces, consistently.
It’s going to be an awesome journey, and I hope you’re as excited as I am to get started!
________________

FILE: 20_Short_VSLs_Lesson_DOC__Short_VSL_Structur_48.txt

﻿Mini VSL Structure #1: Problem → Mechanism → Solution
1. Hook/Problem Callout (10-15 seconds)
   * Direct statement of pain point
   * "If your toe pain is driving you nuts..."
   * "Think you have a small bladder? Think again."
2. Mechanism Reveal (30-60 seconds)
   * Explain the "real cause" most people don't know
   * "Most people don't realize this isn't random. It starts with high uric acid levels..."
   * Scientific/medical explanation made simple
3. Solution Reveal (Without Naming Product In Some Cases) (30-45 seconds)
   * Introduce the natural/different approach
   * Sometimes Mentioning each compound or component + why it’s an important part of an overall solution + potentially other proof elements.
   * Other times, teasing a method or solution without more detail (ie. 7 Second Morning Poop Ritual). 
4. CTA (15-30 seconds)
   * May include Quick Risk reversal or guarantee
   * "If you don't feel the difference, send back the empty bag..."
Mini VSL Structure #2: Biz Opp Contrarian Structure
1. Hook (Contrarian Investment/Income Positioning)
* Traditional [investment/income method] is earning terrible [low %] returns
* People only [do current method] for one reason: they don't know a better way
2. Opportunity Introduction
* "But there's something so much better... it's called [Your Method Name]"
* "Our [students/partners] are earning [X times better] than [traditional method]"
* Quick credibility anchor (verifiable statistic/industry data)
3. Explain Method/System
* Simple example ([physical product/transaction type])
* Key differentiator (why returns are higher - [turnover rate/frequency/leverage])
* Relatable analogy ("Think about it like [familiar concept]...")
* Industry validation ([your industry] is the #1 trending [category])
4. Business Model Reveal
* Partnership structure: "My [business partner] and I partner with [qualifier type] who have [minimum investment amount]"
* What you do for them: "We leverage our [time period] of experience [doing specific thing] for you"
* Done-for-you promise: Build/manage [business type] on your behalf
5. Objection Handling Sequence
* "Why don't you just do it yourself?"
   * We do, but [business model comparison - hedge fund, etc.]
   * Pooling capital allows us to [specific advantage]
   * [OPM concept or similar leverage principle]
* "Is this a scam?"
   * Media credibility ([publications] featured us)
   * [Number] of people we've helped
   * [Specific achievement/recognition]
* "What's the catch?"
   * Limited capacity due to [manual work/personal attention]
   * Can only partner with [small number] of new [partners/students]
6. Qualification Requirements
* Financial qualifier: $[amount]+ [liquid/available]
* Availability scarcity: Extremely limited partnerships
7. Information Gap Bridge
* "I can't explain everything in this [ad/video]"
* Free [case study/workshop/presentation] offer
* Promise more detail than current format allows
8. Primary CTA with Urgency
* Scarcity: "Last time you'll see this [ad/offer]"**
* Motivational push: "If you want things you've never had, try things you've never done"
9. Risk Reversal + Future Pacing
* "What's the worst that could happen?" (Learning about trending industry)
* Timeline future pace: "6-12 months from now, you look back..."
* Success story positioning: "You become our next biggest success story"
10. Final CTA
* Simple action steps: Click → Sign up → Watch
* Casual close: "I'll see you there"

Mini VSL Structure #3: Personal Discovery -> Solution
For Direct Product Sales & Information Products
1. Audience Hook + Life Change Promise
* Audience callout: "[Target audience], pause the scroll for a moment"**
* Big promise: "because what I'm about to tell you can change your life"
* Solution tease: "This is how I [solve specific problem] without doing any of these [common methods]"
2. Problem Agitation (Personal Struggle)
* Failed attempt: "I tried [popular solution] before, but [specific negative consequences]"
* Multiple pain points: [List 2-3 specific frustrations/costs/side effects]
* Emotional impact: "[waste of money/time/health/etc.]"
3. Discovery Moment
* Lucky break: "But luckily, I came across [discovery source - video/article/doctor/friend]"
* What they found: "that was describing [solution type] that could [benefit] without [avoiding negatives]"
4A. Product Reveal Path (For Physical Products)
* Product introduction: "It's called [Product Name]"
* How it works: "and it works by using [technology/mechanism] to [specific function]"
* Key features: "They have [feature 1], [feature 2], [feature 3]"
* Ease of use: "and they [simple activation] as soon as [simple setup]"
4B. Method Tease Path (For Information Products)
* Method name: "It's called the [X]-[Time] [Method Name]"
* What it does: "a [description] way to [solve root cause] and [restore function]"
* What you avoid: "without [conventional treatments/side effects/restrictions]"
* Authority mention: "[Expert type] now call it [validation]"
5. Personal Transformation
* Immediate results: "I can finally [primary benefit] throughout [timeframe]"
* Specific improvements: List 3-4 concrete changes:
   * "And now I [specific improvement] than I have in [timeframe]"
   * "I don't [negative symptom] anymore"
   * "it feels like [positive change]"
   * "My [area of life] has improved"
6A. Direct Sale CTA (For Products)
* Offer: "and right now they're running a special offer for a limited time"
* Action: "Click the link below and get yours before it expires"
6B. Information CTA (For Methods/Rituals)
* Urgency qualifier: "If you're over [age] and experiencing [symptoms]"
* Free information offer: "click below to see [Expert's] [Method Name]"
* Benefit promise: "You could be [desired outcome] and feel [age] years younger"

Mini VSL Structure #4: "Authority/Affinity + Life-Changing Discovery" Template
For Products That Solve Lifestyle/Activity Problems
1. Contrarian Hook + Personal Authority
* Contrarian statement: "Why I'll never [use common solution] for [activity/situation] again"
* Authority/Affinity: "I'm a [profession/hobby/lifestyle/identity that relates to problem]"
2. High-Stakes Situation Setup
* I had an important event or activity coming up. 
* Emotional investment: It was something I’d looked forward to, was nervous about, saved money to participate in, or that just in general was highly important to me. 
3. From Old to New Solution
* I was going to use my old solution, even though it had flaws.
* The switch: "But one day, I swapped my [old solution] for [new solution] and my life changed"
4. Experiencing Benefits From New Solution
* Primary impact: "[Main activity/area] stopped being so hard for me"
* Physical transformation or Deeper transformation: ie. things stopped hurting, I was healthier, I was more confident, people looked at me differently, etc. 
5. Proof/Test Results
* Extreme test: "As a result, in [challenging situation], in [timeframe] I [impressive metric]"
* Pain Point Free proof: "and I didn't even feel a hint of my pain point. 
6. Personal Recommendation
* Authority endorsement: "That's why now I advise everyone to use this [new solution]"
* Broader application (when applicable): "including in their everyday life"
7. Product Authority & Features
* Company credibility: New solution was created by a super credible company. 
* Feature stack: "The new solution/product has [feature 1], [feature 2], [feature 3], and [price benefit]"
8. Comparison/Superiority
* Performance comparison: Products benefits are superior, more effective, last longer than competitors. 
* Additional advantage: Another opportunity to contrast against the old solution. 
9. Technical Benefits
* Additional Key feature: call out a special feature of the product that is particularly important.
* How it works
* Optional Additional features: "They're [practical benefit] and [practical benefit], and they also have [safety feature]"
10. Social Proof
* Target audience validation: "No wonder they have lots of fantastic reviews from [people like target audience] who [face same problem]"
11. Current State Transformation
* Main activity: "Now I can easily do these events/activities/hobbies without pain point.
* Capability expansion: "I'm able to [activity] for hours, and I'm comfortable"
* Specific relief: "No [specific pain point]"
12. Offer + CTA
* Limited offer: "Additionally, they have a limited-time [discount]% off deal if you purchase directly from this link"
* Authority close: "See for yourself why [Product] are considered the leader in their market/region. 
* Simple CTA: "Get yours now"

Mini VSL Structure #5: "Secret" Reveal
(Curiosity-driven - 1-3 minutes)
1. Mystery Hook (15-20 seconds)
   * "Billionaires have a secret..."
   * Reference to hidden knowledge
2. Personal Transformation Story (45-75 seconds)
   * Before state (broke, struggling)
   * Mysterious encounter/discovery
   * Dramatic results
3. Product/Method Reveal (30-45 seconds)
   * What the secret actually is
   * How it works (brief)
4. Urgency CTA (15-20 seconds)
   * Limited availability
   * Act now messaging

Mini VSL Structure #5: Emotional Story
1. Hook/Problem Callout (10 seconds)
* "Shooting pain in your back or sciatica? Do this to relieve joint pain fast."
2. Personal Story as Problem Amplification (45 seconds)
* Dad's golf course collapse
* Medical escalation (pills → shots → surgery)
* Stakes raising (losing mobility completely)
3. Authority-Backed Mechanism Reveal (90 seconds)
* Dr. Kyle Stephens (Harvard-trained) validation
* The "real cause" explanation: liver malfunction → excess inflammation → cartilage destruction
* Scientific detail: synovial fluid, tendons/ligaments, bone-on-bone
* Why conventional treatments fail
4. Solution Introduction with More Authority (45 seconds)
* Dr. Stevenson introduction
* "7 Second Morning Ritual"
* Additional credibility (Boston Celtics team physician)
* Specific discovery (anti-inflammatory compound)
5. Benefits Promise + CTA (30 seconds)
* Future Pacing ("10, 15, even 20 years younger")
* Free presentation offer

Mini VSL Structure #6: Contrarian + Expert Reveals Mechanism

1. Hook + Contrarian Twist (15-25 seconds)
* Benefit Promise: "This [timeframe] [method] can [desired outcome]"
* Contrarian Statement: "Turns out, [common belief] can be just as dangerous as [opposite belief]"
* Pattern Interrupt: "Alarming, right?" / "Surprising, right?" / "Shocking, but true"
2. Authority Setup + Education (Pays Off Contrarian Hook) (20-30 seconds)
* Authority Introduction: "A top [location] [expert type] says that's like [analogy]"
* Reframe: "Most people think [common approach] means [desired outcome]"
* Authority Quote/Analogy: "But [expert] explains it like this..." / "He says that's like [relatable analogy]"
3. Mechanism Reveal with Progressive Explanation (60-90 seconds)
* How It's Supposed to Work: "[System] has a [protective feature] that allows [normal function]"
* What Goes Wrong: "But over time, this [protective feature] gets [damaged/compromised]"
* Body's Failed Solution: "Your body tries to help by [compensating mechanism], but [why it backfires]"
* Escalation Pattern: "It starts in [least noticeable area], then [progression], making [system] [deteriorated state]"
* Symptoms Cascade: "Many folks start feeling [early symptoms], but by then [consequences]"
* Why Common Solutions Fail: "[Popular approach] won't fix the problem. [Popular approach] is like [analogy showing futility]"
4. Real Solution Introduction (30-45 seconds)
* Solution Logic (UMS): "To fix the problem, you need to [actual solution approach]"
* Authority Introduction: "That's why [location] [expert type], [Dr. Name], developed [method name]"
* How It Works: "And when [system] is [restored state], [benefit] naturally [returns/improves]"
* Without Sacrifice: "Without having to [give up favorite things] or [obsess over restrictions]"
* Convenience: "It's so [easy/safe], you can do it [where/when]"
5. Social Proof Story (45-60 seconds)
* Patient Introduction: "One of his patients, [Name] from [Location], tried everything to [solve problem]"
* Failed Attempts: "She [list of failed conventional approaches], but nothing worked"
* Transformation: "Then she tried this [method], and within [timeframe], [authority figure] was amazed"
* Current State: "These days, she [new activities/lifestyle improvements]"
* Broader Proof: "And it's not just [Name]. [Number] of [demographic] are using [Dr. Name's] method"
6. Final CTA with Benefit Stack (25-35 seconds)
* Frustration Acknowledgment: "So if you're tired of [current struggle], if you're frustrated with [failed approaches]"
* Root Cause Promise: "and if you want to address the real cause of [problem]"
* CTA: "tap the button below to see [Dr. Name's] [method description]"
* Expanded Benefits: "that's helping [number] of [demographic] enjoy [lifestyle benefits] into their [age ranges] and beyond"

7. SPG Version of Epic Real Estate Outline
* Hook
* Transformation Story (Guided By Expert Spokesperson from Rock Bottom to Killing It)
* Introduce UMS 
* Explain UMS 
* Results not typical, but what if they were? (Future Pace)
* I can’t teach the UMS fully here, but I created a free presentation/workshop/video. 
* CTA with Urgency
* Remind them of the opportunity
* Final CTA

FILE: 22_VSLs_Landing_vs_InFeed_Lesson_DOC_52.txt

﻿In Feed VSLs vs. On Page VSLs

There are MAJOR DIFFERENCES and it is CRUCIAL you understand this. 

Please watch the two videos associated with this training. One is 11 minutes long and one is 2 minutes long, so it’s not a huge time-suck, but it’s really, really, really, really, really, really, really, really important that you understand this difference. 

In-Feed VSL Structure: 

Hook or Multiple Hooks (Curiosity Heavy) -> Education -> Entertainment (Sometimes) -> Calling Out Pain Point + Promising Solution -> Quick Background Story -> UMP -> UMS -> Product Buildup and Reveal -> Close

Example - Emma Relief’s Meta Video Ads:
https://www.facebook.com/ads/library/?active_status=active&ad_type=all&country=US&is_targeted_country=false&media_type=all&search_type=page&view_all_page_id=105745751961937

Example - Dr. Gundry VSL:
https://app.swipebuilder.io/shares/01JYE6RKQ1D9NAC59NXBQMPGE5?type=PUBLIC&object=SWIPE&require_password=False

On Page VSL Structure:

More often follows classic VSL outline discussed in RMBC.
ESPECIALLY the lead. More about curiosity + calling out pain points, teasing solution, teasing unique mechanism, dropping fascinations, etc. 

Example- Emma Relief On Page VSL: 
https://app.swipebuilder.io/shares/01JYE6HGKPV3XT33CGJ04YGTDH?type=PUBLIC&object=SWIPE&require_password=False

================================================================================

﻿In Feed VSLs vs. On Page VSLs

There are MAJOR DIFFERENCES and it is CRUCIAL you understand this. 

Please watch the two videos associated with this training. One is 11 minutes long and one is 2 minutes long, so it’s not a huge time-suck, but it’s really, really, really, really, really, really, really, really important that you understand this difference. 

In-Feed VSL Structure: 

Hook or Multiple Hooks (Curiosity Heavy) -> Education -> Entertainment (Sometimes) -> Calling Out Pain Point + Promising Solution -> Quick Background Story -> UMP -> UMS -> Product Buildup and Reveal -> Close

Example - Emma Relief’s Meta Video Ads:
https://www.facebook.com/ads/library/?active_status=active&ad_type=all&country=US&is_targeted_country=false&media_type=all&search_type=page&view_all_page_id=105745751961937

Example - Dr. Gundry VSL:
https://app.swipebuilder.io/shares/01JYE6RKQ1D9NAC59NXBQMPGE5?type=PUBLIC&object=SWIPE&require_password=False

On Page VSL Structure:

More often follows classic VSL outline discussed in RMBC.
ESPECIALLY the lead. More about curiosity + calling out pain points, teasing solution, teasing unique mechanism, dropping fascinations, etc. 

Example- Emma Relief On Page VSL:

﻿Brief

1. Who’s the Audience?

2. What are the pain points, or biggest fears?
(+ identify the 1-3 HUGE ones, while the rest are secondary)

- Short Term:

-Long Term:

3. So by reversing the pain points/biggest fears, what is the one big promise (1-3 sentences) you are going to make about the sales copy they’re now reading…how this will change their lives forever?

4. What solutions for the reader’s problem (s) exist already (and why aren’t they working for them)?

5. What’s the new claim/root cause/surprising info? And how does this new solution we’re offering them work? [This is the Unique Mechanism Part]

(Think about it as if they had 99% of the solution already, but you’re sharing that missing 1%...the easy but unexpected REAL REASON, or REAL SECRET to their success).

6. Paradoxical Question:

7. Metaphor:

8. Bold Claim 
(What’s the huge promise about the results they’re going to get using this product/solution?):

9. What is the Product? 
(If you can write out fascinations here, it will help you immensely. This is the part where you get to shape exactly what the product we’re selling will include)

10. Background Story + Story of Discovery: 

11. Some Headline Ideas: 
(One sentence – something that would be the first line of the VSL, or in the copy above the video screen. Attention grabbing)

12. Ideas for a potential upsell product?
(Something that could be sold to the customer immediately after purchasing the main product. You’d want this to be related to product, but solve an additional problem, or provide a significant additional benefit).

FILE: 23_Brief_Old_vs_New_Lesson_DOC__The_New_Brief_DOC_57.txt
================================================================================

﻿Brief

1. Who’s the Audience?

2. What are the pain points, or biggest fears?
(+ identify the 1-3 HUGE ones, while the rest are secondary)

- Short Term:

-Long Term:

3. So by reversing the pain points/biggest fears, what are the big promises you are going to make about the sales copy they’re watching…how this will change their lives forever?
(These are promises about what they will get from interacting with the sales copy, or for teasing a solution you’ll be showing them in the sales copy).

4. What Does It Look Like When A Prospect’s Pain Points Have Been Solved? 
This can include physical, emotional, social and psychological benefits. 

5. What solutions for the reader’s problem (s) exist already (and why aren’t they working for them)?

6. What is the Unique Mechanism of the Problem and the Unique Mechanism of the Solution? 
Please include enough detail so that when given to an LLM, it could write this whole section without struggling.

7. Is There A Unique Nickname for the Unique Mechanism?
This is something that would be teased early on in the lead of the VSL. For example the “7 second bowel releasing ritual” or the “30 second breakfast hack” or “Paper Flipping” to tease a real estate arbitrage method. 

8. (Optional, For Supplements): What are the main ingredients in the formulation. 
For each main ingredient, include 2-3 studies showing their efficacy. 

9. Bold Product Claims
(What’s the huge promise or promises about the results they’re going to get using this product/solution? Note, this is different than the promises from #3. These are now specific promises and claims about how their life will change for the better once they buy the product):

10. What is the Product? 
(This is where we’ll include product details. This might include features and benefits for physical products and programs. It might include fascinations or curiosity bullet teasers for informational programs. The more detail here the better). 

11. Background Story + Story of Discovery: 
This is often a hero's journey structure. The spokesperson or someone the spokesperson knows was in pain. The spokesperson ends up on a quest to find an answer to their pain point. They end up discovering the unique mechanism, why existing solutions don’t work, etc. 

12. Who is the main speaker in the VSL? 
Include a quick snapshot of who they are and their credibility.

13. Is there a second speaker or “expert’ who also has a large role in the VSL?

14. Does the spokesperson partner with a brand or company once they’ve discovered the product? 
If so, please share information about the brand or company here.

15. List of Testimonials or Social Proof If Available

16. Include any Credibility Builders that can be used in the opening of the sales copy. 
This could reference studies about the ingredients, or about the UMP, etc. Perhaps Harvard scientists uncovered the real cause of your problem. Maybe Tony Robbins endorsed this solution? Maybe the program has been featured in Forbes or Good Morning America. Etc.

17. What Is The Normal Retail Price For The Product Being Sold?

18. What Is The Actual Price People Who Watch the VSL Will Pay?

19. If the VSL sells a product with multiple options, what are those options and what is the pricing for each option?

20. What Is The Guarantee?

21. Are There Any Bonuses?
If so please list them out. 

22. Please List Out Any Other Scarcity Elements If There Are Any. 

23. Please Write Out Specific Future-Paced Results and Benefits People Could Expect To Experience After Using the Product.

24. What Are Common Objections Prospects Might Have When Watching the VSL, and How Can We Answer Them?

25. Are there any specific Hooks or Big Ideas that you think should be tested in the lead of the VSL?

﻿Your Job is to Create New Briefs for Copywriting Projects. These are things that I can give to Claude Projects or other LLMs to have them write copy. We’ll mostly be focused on VSLs here, but I may end up asking you to create a brief for an eCommerce page in the future as well.

I’ve included two documents in your knowledge base for now. 

The first is an in-depth brief. It is titled “The New Brief.” 

The second is an outline of the classic Video Sales Letter Structure I’ve used for a long time. That one is mostly for reference. 

Here’s how this will work: 

I will use your chat feature to provide documents that can assist you in writing the brief for a specific product. You’ll then do that. For anything where you don’t have information, you can use placeholders to start.

FILE: 24_Brief_Generator_Claude_Lesson_DOC__VSL_Overview_and_S_60.txt
