﻿Advertorial Outline #1:

Example:
https://get.lubracil.com/Clinician-a

Outline: 
This is a long-form advertorial that does the heavy lifting of selling the product directly, not just selling a click. The structure follows the RMBC Method mapped onto an editorial format :
* Lead → Reader identification + authority hook
* Background Story → Origin, enemy, mechanism destruction
* Unique Mechanism → The "aha" reframe + compound reveal
* Close → Proof, offer, urgency, CTA
The core structure hasn't really changed in years — formats change, but the underlying architecture stays the same.
________________

1. Authority Headline + Alarming Hook
* Credentialed authority figure makes a bold, specific claim
* Pair a fear-inducing statistic with a "but there's hope" promise
* Social proof number to establish scale
* Editorial formatting cues (byline, date, share bar) to maintain native feel
________________

2. Symptom Call-Out + Reader Qualification
* List 3-5 specific, visceral symptoms (sensory language, not clinical abstractions)
* Qualify the reader by demographic or situation
* Direct command to keep reading
* Brief preview of the promise
________________

3. Authority Introduction + "Whistleblower" Positioning
* Name, credentials, experience
* Frame them as going against the establishment
* Name the enemy (industry, big corporations, mainstream medicine)
* Urgency/suppression angle: "this may not stay online"
* Emotional justification for speaking out
________________

4. Origin Story — The Discovery Moment
* Cinematic, specific scene (time, place, sensory detail)
* Authority notices a pattern or finding that changes everything
* Reframe the problem: what the reader THINKS they have vs. what's ACTUALLY happening
* Escalate the severity of the real problem
This is the seed of the Big Idea — the single reframe that the entire advertorial hangs on.
________________

5. Conventional Solution Teardown
* Acknowledge what the reader has probably already tried
* Systematically destroy 3-4 competing solutions:
   * What it does on the surface
   * Why it can't address the root cause
   * Its hidden danger, cost, or dependency trap
* Frame the entire conventional approach as a profit-driven system designed to keep people stuck
Each teardown clears the path for your unique mechanism by eliminating every alternative.
________________

6. Unique Mechanism / Compound Reveal
* Transition from frustration to obsessive research
* Time frame for credibility ("After 2 years of research...")
* Reveal the key ingredient or approach with clinical backing
* Stack 4-6 specific benefits (checkmarks or bullets), each one countering a failure from Section 5
* Deliver the KEY INSIGHT — one sentence that reframes the entire paradigm
That single insight line is the most important sentence in the advertorial. Everything before it builds to this moment. Everything after flows from it.
________________

7. Fear Escalation Framework (Staging or Timeline)
* Break the problem into 3 progressive stages of severity
* Stage 1: Mild, easy to dismiss — "where it started"
* Stage 2: Moderate, accelerating — "where you are NOW" (place the reader here)
* Stage 3: Severe, potentially irreversible — "the point of no return"
* Establish that the reader is in the critical window where action still works
* Make inaction feel like a conscious choice to deteriorate
________________

8. Personal Proof Story (Authority as Patient)
* Authority reveals they experienced the same problem
* List of everything they tried that failed (mirrors reader's journey)
* Emotional toll: shame, isolation, relationship strain
* Decision to test the solution on themselves
* Progressive results timeline:
   * Early signs (Week 1-2)
   * Meaningful improvement (Week 3-4)
   * Emotional breakthrough moment (Week 5-8) — this is the climax
   * Measurable/clinical proof (Week 8-12)
________________

9. Social Proof Cascade
* 3 testimonials, each addressing a different objection:
   * Cost/value objection
   * Safety/side effects objection
   * Severity/"is it too late for me?" objection
* Each includes one specific, believable detail
* Narrative transition: "word spread" or organic demand framing
________________

10. Brand/Mission Story + Trust Stack
* Why they didn't go the corporate/pharmaceutical route
* What a corporate partner would have ruined (diluted formula, fillers, higher price, prescription barrier)
* Quality proof points stacked with checkmarks:
   * Sourcing, dosage, purity, testing, manufacturing standards
________________

11. Mechanism Deep Dive — How It Works (3-Step System)
* 3 numbered steps, each with:
   * A benefit-oriented name
   * An accessible analogy
   * A connection back to a specific symptom from Section 2
* Frame the product as a "system" rather than a single-action solution
________________

12. Offer, Risk Reversal, Final CTA
* Pricing and bundle options
* Savings framing (per-day cost, comparison to conventional solutions)
* Strong guarantee with specific terms
* Final urgency callback to the staging framework from Section 7
* FAQ addressing remaining objections
* Clear, direct CTA
________________

How to Use This
This is your canvas. You don't have to include every single section, and depending on the product or market sophistication, you might compress or expand certain parts. The non-negotiables are:
1. The Big Idea reframe (Section 4) — without this, nothing else matters
2. The conventional solution teardown (Section 5) — this is what makes your mechanism feel like the ONLY answer
3. The personal proof story with an emotional climax (Section 8) — this is what makes people buy
Everything else supports those three pillars.

________________

Advertorial Outline #2

Example:
https://info.clarifionodrx.com/odrx/meta/lp1/?utm_source=facebook&utm_medium=paidsocial&utm_content=%7B%7Badset.id%7D%7D&lpv=Clarifion-ODRx-Meta-LP1(PM-GIF-V3)-09-13-24

Outline: 
Alright, this is a very different animal than the Lubracil one. Let me break down why before we get into the outline.
The Lubracil advertorial was a long-form "Clinician Exposé" — essentially a full sales letter disguised as a medical article. It did ALL the selling.
This Clarifion one is a medium-length advertorial that sits behind video ads. The video ads are already doing 1-2 minutes of problem agitation, product reveal, and mechanism education before the reader ever hits this page. So the advertorial doesn't need to do as much heavy lifting on the discovery/mechanism side — it needs to reinforce, expand, and close.
The structure is fundamentally different. Let's abstract it.
________________

Medium-Length Advertorial Outline: "Problem Amplifier + Product Showcase" Framework (Generalized)
Best for: Physical products, devices, gadgets, or solutions where the product has already been partially introduced via a video ad or pre-sell. The advertorial's job is to deepen the problem, establish the mechanism, stack proof, and drive to an offer page.
________________

1. Symptom-Loaded Headline
* Pack the headline with 3-4 specific, visceral symptoms
* Name the solution type without necessarily naming the product
* Promise framing: "Here's Why" or "Here's What to Do"
* The headline alone should make the reader think "that's exactly my life"
Key difference from the Clinician Exposé: No authority figure in the headline. This leads with the reader's pain, not a doctor's credentials. It's a Problem/Solution Lead rather than a Story Lead.
________________

2. Editorial Framing Bar
* Fake publication name relevant to the niche
* Breadcrumb navigation (Home > Trending > Products)
* This is short but critical — it sets the "editorial content" frame before the reader's skepticism kicks in
________________

3. "Don't Stop Reading" Hook
* 1-2 sentence italicized or bolded note
* Tells the reader their life will change after reading this
* Creates micro-commitment to keep scrolling
________________

4. Problem Amplification — Symptom Stack + Hidden Danger
* Call out the primary sensory experience of the problem (what they see, smell, feel)
* Normalize it: "This isn't unusual, especially if you [common situation]"
* Then ESCALATE: reveal that the obvious problem is actually masking a more dangerous underlying issue
* Stack the health/lifestyle consequences:
   * Immediate physical symptoms (3-4 bullets)
   * Impact on others in the household (family, pets, guests)
   * Social embarrassment angle
* Close with a teaser: "Here's how to fix it without [effort/cost]..."
This section does what the video ad started but goes deeper. It takes the problem from "annoying" to "dangerous and embarrassing."
________________

5. Root Cause Reveal
* Transition: "If you don't target the root cause..."
* Name the actual underlying cause (not the surface symptom)
* Explain WHY the root cause is so persistent (e.g., microscopic, invisible, self-perpetuating)
* Escalate to worst-case: potential for permanent or irreversible damage
* This reframe is the closest thing to a Big Idea in this format — it shifts from "I have an annoying problem" to "there's an invisible threat in my home"
________________

6. Conventional Solution Teardown (Compressed)
* Unlike the Clinician Exposé which tears down 3-4 solutions in detail, this version does a quick 1-2 sentence dismissal
* Name the obvious thing people try
* Explain in one line why it doesn't address the root cause
* Transition: "You need to directly address [the root cause], and that's where this comes in..."
This is compressed because the video ad has likely already planted seeds of doubt about conventional solutions.
________________

7. Product Introduction + Social Proof Anchor
* Name the brand/product
* Brief origin or "took the market by storm" narrative
* Anchor with a massive social proof number (reviews, units sold, media mentions)
* This is NOT the mechanism explanation yet — it's purely positioning the product as credible and in-demand before explaining how it works
________________

8. "Nose-Blind" Pattern Interrupt (Unexpected Angle)
* Introduce a surprising statistic or concept the reader hasn't considered
* This serves as a pattern interrupt in the middle of the advertorial to re-engage attention
* It also introduces a NEW dimension of the problem they hadn't thought about
* Deepens the embarrassment/social proof angle
This is a smart structural move. Just when the reader might be losing steam, you hit them with something unexpected that makes the problem feel even worse than they realized.
________________

9. Mechanism Explanation (Accessible)
* Explain HOW the product works in simple, benefit-oriented terms
* Use "magic" or "breakthrough" framing to build intrigue
* Then immediately follow with a plain-English explanation
* Contrast it against conventional approaches:
   * Conventional: masks/covers the symptom
   * This product: eliminates at the source
* Key differentiators stacked as bullets (no filters, no maintenance, no chemicals, works 24/7, etc.)
Keep this shorter than in the Clinician Exposé. You're explaining just enough for the reader to believe the mechanism is real and different — not giving a PhD-level breakdown.
________________

10. Benefit Expansion — "But Wait, It Does More"
* Reveal that the product solves ADDITIONAL problems beyond the primary one
* Stack 2-3 secondary benefits
* Connect back to health/quality of life
* This widens the value perception and justifies higher price points or bundle purchases
________________

11. Lifestyle Transformation Paint
* Short paragraph painting the "after" picture
* Focus on relief, freedom, confidence
* Include family/social benefits: guests coming over, no more embarrassment
* "It's like having a [guardian/protector/shield] working 24/7"
________________

12. Personal Story / Mini-Testimonial
* One specific person's story (can be the author or a friend)
* Brief: the problem, how bad it got, the product fixed it
* Emotional detail but keep it to 3-5 short paragraphs
* This isn't the epic 4-phase timeline from the Clinician Exposé — it's a quick proof hit
________________

13. Usage Recommendation + Bundle Justification
* Specific recommendation: "For best results, use [multiple units / daily / etc.]"
* Tie the recommendation to the reader's specific situation (e.g., "If you have [X situation], you need [Y amount]")
* This is pre-selling the bundle before they even see the offer page
* Frame it as data-driven: "After evaluating [X] customer success stories..."
________________

14. Offer Teaser + Discount Reveal
* "An exceptional offer awaits you on the next page"
* Specific discount (up to X% off)
* Free shipping
* Guarantee mention (satisfaction guarantee with specific timeframe)
* Stack the "no ongoing cost" angle if applicable (no filters, no refills, no subscriptions)
________________

15. Trust Badges / Certifications
* 2-4 trust seals or certification logos
* Brief one-liner about what each represents
* This is visual more than textual — quick credibility hit before the CTA
________________

16. Urgency Close + Final CTA
* Stock scarcity or pricing scarcity ("once current stock runs out, we can't maintain this price")
* External justification for scarcity (market instability, supply chain, etc.)
* Star rating + review count as final social proof
* Bold, clear CTA button
* Reiterate the discount and what they're getting
________________

Key Structural Differences from the "Clinician Exposé" Framework
Element
	Clinician Exposé
	Problem Amplifier
	Length
	2,000-3,000+ words
	1,200-1,800 words
	Authority figure
	Central to the entire piece
	Absent or minimal
	Lead type
	Story Lead / Authority Lead
	Problem-Solution Lead
	Mechanism depth
	Deep dive with 3-step system
	Quick explanation, benefit-focused
	Conventional teardown
	Extensive (3-4 solutions destroyed)
	Compressed (1-2 quick dismissals)
	Proof structure
	Epic personal timeline + 3 testimonials
	Quick story + social proof numbers
	Fear framework
	3-stage escalation system
	Root cause reveal + worst-case mention
	Pre-sell assumption
	Cold traffic, no prior exposure
	Warm traffic from video ad
	Primary job
	Does ALL the selling
	Reinforces and closes the sale
	Offer location
	Embedded in the advertorial
	Teased, then delivered on next page
	________________

When to Use This Framework
Use the Problem Amplifier when:
* You have a video ad doing the initial hook and product introduction
* Your product is tangible/physical and easy to understand visually
* The mechanism is simple enough to explain in a few sentences
* You're driving to a separate product/checkout page rather than selling directly in the advertorial
* Your audience is problem-aware but may not fully grasp the severity
Use the Clinician Exposé when:
* Traffic is colder and hasn't been pre-sold
* The mechanism is complex and needs extensive education
* You need the authority angle for credibility (health, medical, financial)
* The advertorial IS the sales page — it needs to do all the heavy lifting

Advertorial Outline #3

Example:
https://alphainfuse.com/pages/alphainfuse-lsticle-lp

Outline: 
Alright, this is a great example of a completely different advertorial format. The listicle is one of the most versatile structures out there, especially for Meta traffic where you need to match the casual, content-consumption mindset people are in when scrolling. Let me break down the generalized framework.
________________
Listicle Advertorial Outline: "X Reasons Why" Framework (Generalized)
Best for: Products where you need to overcome skepticism from people who've tried multiple competing solutions and failed. Works especially well when your product has a clear mechanical or experiential differentiator. This format thrives on Meta and native traffic because it looks and feels like content, not advertising.
________________
1. Urgency / Offer Bar (Sticky or Top-of-Page)
* Guarantee callout (risk reversal leading)
* Free shipping mention
* Limited time discount with specific percentage
* CTA button visible before they read a single word
* This bar often stays sticky on scroll — the offer is always one click away
Why this matters: Unlike the other two frameworks where the offer comes at the END of the journey, the listicle puts the offer in the reader's peripheral vision from the very first second. The content below is essentially giving them permission to click what's already right there.
________________
2. Listicle Headline
* Format: "[Number] Reasons Why [Impressive Social Proof Number] [Target Audience] Are Ditching [Old Solutions] for [Product/Brand]"
* Subhead: One sentence that names the core insight — why everything else failed
Anatomy of this headline structure:
* Number: Creates a concrete, finite commitment ("I just need to read 7 things")
* Social proof number: Establishes herd behavior before a single claim is made
* "Ditching X for Y": Positions it as a migration, not a gamble — other people have already made this switch
* Subhead reframe: Seeds the mechanism without explaining it yet
________________

3. Empathy Opening + Problem Framework
* 2-3 sentences that mirror the reader's exact journey ("You've tried X, Y, Z...")
* Name specific products/approaches they've already failed with
* Validate their frustration: "We get it"
* Then deliver the INSIGHT — name the 2-3 fundamental reasons everything else fails
* Transition: "Here's exactly why thousands are making the switch"
This is your entire Reader section compressed into one short paragraph. No story, no cinematic scene, no authority figure — just "I see you, I know what you've been through, and here's why none of it worked."
________________
4. Social Proof Anchors (Repeated Throughout)
* Sprinkled between sections, not just at the end
* Two key proof points repeated in slightly different formats:
   * Number of users/customers
   * "No side effects / no hassle" promise
* These act as pattern interrupts and trust reinforcements between the list items
Repetition is intentional. Every time the reader's skepticism starts to rebuild, another trust anchor knocks it back down.
________________
5. The List Items (The Core Structure)
This is where the magic is. Each list item follows a specific formula, but not every item needs every element. The key is variation within a consistent structure so it doesn't feel robotic.
List Item Formula:
Title: Benefit-oriented statement that contrasts with the old way Format: "[Positive Outcome] (Unlike/Where [Old Solution] Fails)" The Problem: 1-2 sentences naming the specific failure of conventional approaches The Solution: 1-2 sentences explaining how this product solves it differently Testimonial (on select items): Short, specific, star-rated review with name and age CTA Block (on select items): Offer reminder + button
How to Structure Your 5-7 List Items:
Not every list item carries the same weight. Here's the role each one plays: Item 1 — The Mechanism Differentiator
* This is your LEAD item and it carries the most weight
* Explains the fundamental mechanical/scientific reason this product works differently
* Pairs with a testimonial that specifically validates the mechanism
* Longest item in the list
Item 2 — The Convenience/Compliance Advantage
* Addresses the "I couldn't stick with it" objection
* Compares the effort required vs. competing solutions
* Specific: name exact time commitment, frequency, steps involved
* First CTA block appears after this item
Item 3 — The "Holy Grail" Result
* Names the ONE result that competitors can't deliver
* Testimonial here should be the most emotionally compelling
* This is your aspirational peak — the result they've given up hoping for
Item 4 — The Clinical/Credibility Proof
* Reference studies, clinical data, or head-to-head comparisons
* "Outperformed [well-known competitor] in clinical studies"
* This doesn't need to be long — the specificity of the claim does the work
* Can be the shortest item in the list
Item 5 — The Sensory/Experience Advantage
* Addresses what it FEELS like to use the product day-to-day
* Contrasts with the unpleasant experience of competing solutions
* Targets the "ugh" factor that made them quit previous solutions
Item 6 — The Fear Eliminator
* Names the #1 fear or side effect keeping them from acting
* Directly and explicitly states this product doesn't have that problem
* This is pure objection destruction — no selling, just removing the barrier
Item 7 — The Risk Reversal
* Guarantee details framed as a "reason to try"
* Specific timeframe and terms
* Positions the guarantee as confidence in the product, not a sales tactic
________________

6. Final Proof Block + Emotional Close
* "Join [number] [people] who've finally found [the solution]"
* Reinforce "no side effects, no hassle, no empty promises"
* This is the community/belonging close — you're not buying a product, you're joining a movement of people who figured it out
________________

7. Final CTA + Trust Stack
* Bold CTA button with risk-free language
* Guarantee reiterated with specific days
* Trust badges / payment security icons
* Contact information (email, phone) for legitimacy
* Clean footer with policy links
________________

The Psychology Behind the Listicle Structure
The reason this works so well — and why it's become one of the most common advertorial formats on Meta — is that it maps perfectly to how skeptical buyers process information:
1. "I've tried everything" → Empathy opening validates their experience
2. "Why should this be different?" → Item 1 gives them the mechanism answer
3. "Sounds good but is it a hassle?" → Item 2 eliminates friction
4. "Can it really deliver THE result I want?" → Item 3 shows the aspirational proof
5. "Where's the evidence?" → Item 4 delivers clinical credibility
6. "What's the catch?" → Items 5-6 eliminate the hidden downsides
7. "What if it doesn't work for me?" → Item 7 removes all risk
Each list item knocks down exactly one objection. By the time they reach the end, there's nothing left to object to. That's the whole game.
________________
When to Use the Listicle Framework
* Your audience is solution-aware — they know products exist, they've tried them, they're skeptical
* You have multiple clear differentiators (not just one mechanism story)
* Your product has a convenience or experience advantage over competitors
* You're running Meta traffic where content-style formats outperform editorial-style ones
* You want a shorter, faster-moving advertorial that doesn't require deep storytelling
When NOT to Use It
* Your audience is problem-unaware and needs education about WHY they have the problem
* Your mechanism is complex and requires a deep narrative to explain
* You're selling something where authority/credibility is the primary purchase driver
* The product doesn't have clear, listable differentiators vs. the competition
________________
 That gives you three frameworks now — the Clinician Exposé, the Problem Amplifier, and the Listicle. Three very different structures for three very different traffic situations and product types. Drop the next one whenever you're ready.

Advertorial Outline #4

Example:
https://rejuveen.com/pages/ps-uflora-listicle-infection-pt?fbclid=IwY2xjawPTbPFleHRuA2FlbQIxMABicmlkETFFZkg1OVc3dXgwamJaZ3A3c3J0YwZhcHBfaWQPNTQxNjM5NDkzODg5MDI1AAEeBAK-aojyChxWKzh8ei1o8DQvoaHZSdWektvowTcywVtAjb-E6LgOfrjW_1o_aem_Vc5bXB7NTPJEcmbPweG-CA#problem

Outline: 
Alright, this is a really interesting one because it's doing something the other three frameworks don't — it's combining the educational, story-driven content of an advertorial with the conversion architecture of a product detail page (PDP). It's a hybrid, and it's smart because it eliminates the friction of clicking through to a separate page. Let me break down the generalized framework.
________________
Listicle/PDP Hybrid Advertorial Outline: "Story-Driven Listicle with Embedded Checkout" Framework (Generalized)
Best for: Supplement and health products where you need to do heavy education AND close the sale on the same page. This format works when you want the depth of a long-form advertorial, the scannable structure of a listicle, and the conversion power of a PDP — all in one URL. It eliminates the drop-off that happens when you send people from an advertorial to a separate product page.
________________
1. Sticky Offer Bar + Embedded Checkout (Always Present)
* Guarantee callout
* Free shipping threshold
* The actual product purchasing module (quantity selector, pricing tiers, add-to-cart) is embedded ON the page — not on a separate PDP
* Multiple pricing tiers visible:
   * Single unit (highest per-unit cost)
   * Mid bundle with savings callout
   * Best value bundle with largest savings + "Best Value" badge
* One-time purchase reassurance ("All orders are one-time purchase only")
This is the defining structural difference. In a standard listicle, you're selling the click to another page. In this hybrid, the checkout IS the page. The reader can buy at any point without leaving. This is exactly what I've talked about with the Clarifion example — when you combine the advertorial and PDP, your CPA drops and your AOV goes up because you're not losing people in the handoff.
________________
2. Benefit-Loaded Headline + Mechanism Subhead
* Headline names the specific, desirable end result (not the product name)
* Format: "[Action Verb] [Specific Problem] & [Restores/Delivers] [Specific Measurable Outcome]"
* Below the headline, a listicle-style subhead:
   * "[Number] Ways [Product] [Achieves Headline Promise]"
* This dual-headline structure does two jobs: the top line hooks on desire, the bottom line creates a scannable content framework
________________

3. Doctor Dialogue Opening (Story Lead with Authority)
* Opens with a direct quote from a named medical professional
* Conversational, scene-setting tone — you're IN the doctor's office
* Specific sensory details (squeaking chair, leaning in close)
* The doctor reframes the problem with a new, more accurate name
* Delivers a shocking stat: "90% of doctors have never heard of this"
* Creates an enemy: the medical establishment's approach is fundamentally wrong
This is a compressed version of the Clinician Exposé opening, but delivered as DIALOGUE rather than narrative. It moves faster because you're reading a conversation, not an article. The reader becomes a fly on the wall in the exam room.
________________
4. Visual Mechanism Breakdown (The Doctor's Drawing)
* The authority breaks the problem into 3-4 sequential steps
* Each step is numbered and simple — one sentence each
* Visual metaphor: "drew three circles," "showed me a diagram"
* The sequence reveals a vicious cycle where the conventional treatment actually makes the problem worse
* Ends with the emotional gut-punch question: "You're saying [the thing I've been doing] actually makes it WORSE?"
This is your Mechanism section, but disguised as a doctor explaining something on a whiteboard. The numbered steps make a complex biological process feel simple and inevitable.
________________
5. Emotional Gut-Punch + Gender/Dismissal Anger Beat
* Reader/narrator has an emotional reaction (tears, anger, disbelief)
* Specific time frame of suffering ("Two years of...")
* Stack 3 visceral emotional experiences
* Introduce a COMPARISON that triggers righteous anger — how a similar problem in a different context gets immediate, respectful treatment while THIS problem gets dismissed
* The dismissive advice they received ("try yogurt," "better hygiene")
* End with a quiet, desperate question: "So what's the solution?"
This is pure emotional engineering. You're not just making them sad — you're making them ANGRY. Anger is a much more powerful purchase motivator than sadness because angry people take action. The gender comparison beat is especially powerful in women's health because it taps into a real, lived frustration.
________________
6. Transition to Listicle
* One line: "Here's how [Product] fixes all [number] problems at once — and delivers bonus benefits you'll love"
* This single sentence bridges the emotional story into the structured listicle
* The "bonus benefits" tease keeps them reading past the core promise
________________

7. The Listicle Items (Core Structure)
Each list item follows a consistent but varied formula. Here's the pattern:
Individual List Item Formula:
Title: Action-oriented benefit statement Format: "[Action Verb] Your [Specific System/Function]" Personal Emotional Scene: 1-3 sentences of first-person narrative describing the EXPERIENCE of the problem — not clinical language, but visceral, sensory, emotionally raw moments. This is what separates this framework from the standard listicle — every benefit is anchored to a specific painful memory. Ingredient/Mechanism Proof: Named, trademarked ingredients with specific clinical data points:
* Exact percentages ("cuts harmful bacteria by 99.07%")
* Exact timeframes ("colonizes in just 7 days")
* Named studies or measurement methods
"Why It Matters" Bridge: One sentence translating the science into plain English — why THIS ingredient works where generic alternatives fail Shocking Stat (on select items): A research-backed data point that reframes the problem's severity Testimonials (2 per item): Short, specific, emotionally vivid quotes with real names
How to Structure Your 5 List Items:
Item 1 — The Core Mechanism Fix
* This carries the most scientific weight
* Named, trademarked ingredients with specific clinical percentages
* "Why it matters" line that explains why everything else fails at this step
* Shocking stat about how the conventional approach is wrong
* 2 testimonials focused on the PRIMARY symptom disappearing
* This is the longest item
Item 2 — The Protective Barrier Rebuild
* Shifts from "killing the bad" to "building the good"
* References FDA-acknowledged claims for extra credibility
* 1 testimonial focused on the day-to-day improvement
Item 3 — The Environment Restoration
* Addresses the invisible underlying condition (pH, microbiome, inflammation)
* Specific measurable ranges (what's dangerous vs. healthy)
* Explains the self-sustaining cycle the product creates
* 1 testimonial with a specific timeline of improvement
Item 4 — The Hidden Driver (Stress/Hormonal/Immune)
* Reveals a surprising SECONDARY cause most people don't know about
* Named adaptogen or secondary ingredient with specific data
* Multiple measurable outcomes (cortisol reduction %, desire increase %, etc.)
* This item expands the product's value beyond the primary problem
* 2 testimonials — one focused on the hidden driver, one on relationship impact
Item 5 — The Lifestyle/Emotional Transformation
* Shifts from clinical to emotional
* Stack of 3-4 specific embarrassing moments the reader will recognize
* Testimonials focused on confidence, freedom, and normalcy returning
* This is the aspirational close of the listicle section
________________

8. Warning Signs Interstitial (Fear Reactivation)
* After the listicle's positive momentum, PAUSE and reintroduce fear
* List 5-6 specific warning signs with alarm emoji/icons
* Each sign is concrete and testable (not vague)
* Close with escalation: "Every cycle you let go untreated makes it harder to beat"
This is strategically placed AFTER the solution has been fully explained. The reader now knows the fix exists, which makes the fear of NOT acting much more acute. You're not scaring them into hopelessness — you're scaring them into action.
________________
9. Transformation Timeline
* Break results into 4 progressive phases:
   * Weeks 1-2: First noticeable symptom relief
   * Weeks 3-4: Primary symptoms resolve
   * Weeks 5-8: Full symptom relief + secondary benefits emerge
   * Weeks 9-12: Complete restoration / maintenance phase
* This sets realistic expectations AND justifies the 90-day bundle purchase
* The timeline should map to the bundle they want to sell the most
Notice: The timeline duration perfectly matches the "Best Value" bundle. That's not an accident. You're engineering the clinical narrative to justify the highest AOV option.
________________
10. First Checkout Block (Mid-Page)
* Special offer callout with specific savings
* Checkmark stack of trust points:
   * Money-back guarantee with specific days
   * Manufacturing credentials (Made in USA, FDA-registered facility)
   * Ingredient quality (100% natural)
   * Safety compatibility (safe with other medications)
   * Social proof number
   * Per-day cost comparison ("less than your morning coffee")
   * Anti-scam reassurances (no auto-billing, free shipping)
* 1 testimonial about regret for not starting sooner (creates urgency)
________________

11. Future Pacing / Visualization Close
* "Imagine in just [timeframe]:" followed by 4-5 specific lifestyle moments
* Each moment directly mirrors a painful moment from the listicle items
* Escalate from practical relief to emotional/identity transformation
* Close with urgency: "Every day you wait lets [the problem] dig deeper"
* Identity statement: "You bring HER back" — frame the purchase as reclaiming who they really are
This is aspirational close meets urgency close. You're simultaneously showing them the life they want AND making them feel the cost of delay.
________________
12. Second Checkout Block (Bottom of Page)
* Identical purchasing module to the top
* Free shipping threshold reminder
* Discount auto-applied messaging
* Guarantee reiterated per bundle option
________________

13. Authority Endorsement Section
* 2-3 named medical professionals with credentials and photos
* Each endorsement hits a different angle:
   * Endorsement 1: Broad wellness positioning (digestion, urinary, stress)
   * Endorsement 2: Specialist credibility (women's health nurse)
   * Endorsement 3: Personal experience + professional recommendation
* "As seen in" media logos for additional credibility
________________

14. Testimonial Waterfall
* 8-12+ additional testimonials in a scrollable or grid format
* Mix of:
   * Primary benefit testimonials
   * Unexpected bonus benefit testimonials (appetite, weight, nails)
   * Relationship/intimacy testimonials
   * Long-time sufferer testimonials
* Include variety of ages and situations
* Photos where possible
________________

15. FAQ Section
* 6-8 questions addressing:
   * How it works (mechanism recap)
   * Timeline expectations
   * Safety/interactions
   * Guarantee details
   * Shipping/billing
   * "Will it work for MY specific situation?"
* Each answer is 2-3 sentences, benefit-oriented, not defensive
________________

16. Final CTA + Third Checkout Block
* Last chance urgency messaging
* Final trust stack
* Third embedded checkout module
________________

Why the Hybrid Works Better Than Listicle → Separate PDP
This is the key insight, and it's exactly what I've been teaching : When you send someone from a listicle to a separate PDP, you lose people at the transition. They click through, see a product page that looks like every other product page, and their emotional momentum dies. The story stops. The spell breaks. The hybrid keeps the reader inside the story from first scroll to checkout. The emotional narrative and the purchasing decision happen in the same continuous experience. By the time they reach the checkout module, they've already been sold — they just need to pick their bundle size. The three checkout blocks (top, middle, bottom) mean that whether someone is a fast decision-maker who just needs the headline and offer, a moderate reader who converts after the listicle, or a deep reader who needs every testimonial and FAQ — there's a checkout waiting for them exactly when they're ready.
________________
Key Structural Differences: All Four Frameworks
Element
	Clinician Exposé
	Problem Amplifier
	Standard Listicle
	Listicle/PDP Hybrid
	Length
	2,500-3,500+ words
	1,200-1,800 words
	1,500-2,000 words
	2,500-4,000+ words
	Lead type
	Story/Authority
	Problem-Solution
	Social Proof/List
	Story/Authority + List
	Checkout location
	Embedded in page
	Separate product page
	Separate product page
	Embedded on same page (3x)
	Emotional depth
	Very high (epic story)
	Moderate
	Low-moderate
	Very high (personal scenes per item)
	Mechanism depth
	Deep 3-step system
	Quick explanation
	One item per differentiator
	Doctor dialogue + ingredient proof per item
	Authority presence
	Central narrator
	Absent/minimal
	Absent
	Opening scene + endorsement section
	Testimonial strategy
	3 strategic testimonials
	Social proof numbers
	1 per list item
	2 per list item + waterfall section
	Urgency structure
	3-stage fear framework
	Root cause + worst case
	Minimal
	Warning signs + timeline + future pacing
	AOV optimization
	Bundle offer at end
	Teased, sold on next page
	Sold on next page
	Multiple bundle blocks throughout
	Best traffic temp
	Cold
	Warm (post-video)
	Warm (Meta feed)
	Cold to warm
	________________
 That's four complete frameworks now for the RMBC II members. Each one serves a different strategic purpose depending on traffic temperature, product complexity, and where you want the sale to happen. Let me know if you want me to refine any of these or create fill-in-the-blank templates for any of them.

﻿Prompt #1: 

I want your help doing competitor research for a product in the YOUR NICHE space. The specific product is _PRODUCT_and we are focused on competitors in _GEOGRAPHY_. 

Specifically, we’re looking for D2C brands who primarily sell online through eCommerce or Direct Response sales funnels. 

For each competitor you find, I want to understand:
Who is the target demo they speak to?
What are their main new customer acquisition funnels?
What is their core messaging in their ads, advertorials, and other advertising assets? 
What are examples of their advertisements or landing page assets if available?
Are there any recurring or repetitive hooks/angles/big ideas you see consistently appearing in their advertising assets?
What is their pricing structure?
What do customers love and what do customers dislike about them (use reviews, social signals, social media platforms, etc to answer this)? 
If available, what is their estimated overall business revenue and revenue for their hero product(s) that are most similar to the one I’ve mentioned?

Optional:
Here are more details about the market _DETAILS_

Please go ahead and get started now, and thank you!

=================================

What is their core messaging in their ads, advertorials, and other advertising assets?

Here are more details about the market _let’s focus on skincare for women here. 

Please go ahead and get started now, and thank you!

FILE: 41_Meta_Ads_Lesson_DOC_99.txt

﻿Meta Ads

Overarching Idea: 
* You can’t talk about ads without assets. 
* You can’t get around testing

What is the Objective?
* Acquire New Customers?
* Generate New Leads?
* Sell The Solution?
* Sell the Click?
* Increase Brand and Product Awareness?

* What is the Product/Market Awareness Level?
Unaware: Prospects are not even aware of a problem or need that your product or service can solve.

   * Problem Aware: Prospects recognize they have a problem or need but are unaware of potential solutions.

   * Solution Aware: Prospects know that solutions exist for their problem, but they are not yet aware of your specific solution.

   * Product Aware: Prospects know about your solution, your product or service, and are evaluating its features and benefits. OR, the at least know about nearly identical solutions/products/services.

   * Most Aware: Prospects are highly aware of your solution, its benefits, and are likely to make a purchase decision soon. 

Where Do We Send People?
   * Send people to an Advertorial?
   * Send people to a VSL?
   * Send people to a long PDP?
   * Send people to a short PDP?
   * Brand building and awareness?
   * Registration/Signup Page

What is the Format?
      * Ultra Short Video?
      * Short Video?
      * Medium Video?
      * Long Video?
      * Static?

Commonalities?
      * Curiosity 
      * Visuals
      * Education
      * Emotional
      * Social Proof (UGC/Testimonials/Etc)
      * ???

Native:

* Native audience ready to consume
* Classic funnel is through an advertorial 
* No targeting, Ads will have to do the job
* Audience older (~55)

* Limited inventory

﻿Deep Research Prompt
Ultimate Universal Target Avatar Deep Research Prompt
CONTEXT: I need you to analyze [WEBSITE URL] and conduct comprehensive target avatar research for this business. First, visit their website and understand their product/service, value proposition, target market, pricing, and unique positioning. Then provide detailed answers about their ideal target avatar so I can create the most profitable ads possible.
YOUR MISSION: After analyzing the business website, answer ALL of the following questions with specific, actionable insights about their ideal customer avatar:
BUSINESS ANALYSIS FOUNDATION
1. What is this business's core product/service offering and primary value proposition?
2. What industry/market do they operate in, and what's their unique positioning vs. competitors?
3. What pricing model and tier does this business operate in (budget, mid-market, premium, luxury)?
DEMOGRAPHICS & FOUNDATION
4. What are the specific demographic details (age range, gender, income level, education, location, family status) of their ideal customer?
5. What life stage, career level, or business situation is this avatar typically in when they need this solution?
6. Are they B2B or B2C focused, and what's their decision-making role (individual consumer, business owner, department head, etc.)?
PAIN POINTS & CHALLENGES
7. What are the top 3-5 specific problems or pain points this avatar experiences that this business solves?
8. What are the emotional and psychological frustrations they feel when dealing with these challenges?
9. What have they tried before to solve these issues, and why didn't those solutions work?
10. What happens if they don't solve this problem (consequences, missed opportunities, continued frustration)?
GOALS & MOTIVATIONS
11. What are their primary goals and desired outcomes over the next 1-3 years related to this problem area?
12. What specific metrics, results, or life improvements do they use to measure success?
13. What motivates them to take action - avoiding pain, gaining pleasure, achieving status, improving efficiency, or something else?
14. What would their ideal end state look like after using this product/service?
DECISION-MAKING PROCESS
15. How does this avatar typically research and evaluate solutions in this category before making decisions?
16. Who else is involved in their decision-making process (family, colleagues, bosses, advisors)?
17. What objections or concerns typically prevent them from purchasing solutions like this?
18. What's their typical buying timeline from problem awareness to purchase decision?
COMMUNICATION & BEHAVIOR
19. Where does this avatar spend their time online and offline (social platforms, websites, communities, physical locations)?
20. What language, terminology, and communication style resonates most with them?
21. What time of day/week are they most likely to engage with content or make purchasing decisions?
22. How do they prefer to be communicated with (email, social media, phone, in-person, etc.)?
CURRENT SOLUTIONS & COMPETITIVE LANDSCAPE
23. What alternatives, competitors, or current solutions are they using to address their needs?
24. What would make them switch from their current approach to this business's solution?
25. What do they like/dislike about existing options in this market?
26. How do they currently measure or track results in this area?
VALUE PERCEPTION & PREFERENCES
27. How do they prefer to consume information about solutions in this category (video, text, demos, trials, consultations)?
28. What would they consider a "quick win" vs. a long-term strategic investment?
29. What's their typical budget range and buying cycle for solutions in this price category?
30. How price-sensitive are they, and what factors justify higher prices to them?
VALIDATION & SPECIFICITY
31. Can you provide specific real examples of companies/people who perfectly represent this avatar?
32. What does their typical day look like, and when does this problem/need surface?
33. What other products/services do they typically buy that indicate they're ideal for this business?
PSYCHOLOGICAL TRIGGERS & EMOTIONAL DRIVERS
34. What specific words, phrases, or emotional triggers instantly grab their attention in marketing?
35. What are their deepest fears and anxieties related to this problem area?
36. What are their secret desires and aspirations they might not openly admit?
37. What status symbols, social proof elements, or peer validation do they value most?
38. What time-sensitive urgency naturally exists in their world related to this need?
BUYING PSYCHOLOGY & BEHAVIOR
39. Are they impulse buyers or deliberate researchers, and what's their typical decision timeline?
40. What's the maximum amount they've ever spent on similar solutions, and what justified that investment?
41. What specific outcomes, ROI, or improvements would make price irrelevant to them?
42. Do they prefer to be early adopters or wait for social proof from others?
43. What buying triggers have successfully motivated them in past purchases (scarcity, social proof, authority, reciprocity)?
MEDIA CONSUMPTION & ATTENTION PATTERNS
44. What specific influencers, thought leaders, publications, or brands do they follow and trust?
45. What type of content format gets them to stop and engage vs. scroll past?
46. What device and platform do they primarily use when researching solutions like this?
47. What's their attention span for different types of content related to this topic?
48. When are they most receptive to marketing messages (time of day, day of week, seasonally)?
COMPETITIVE INTELLIGENCE & POSITIONING
49. What competitor marketing messages or positioning have they responded to recently?
50. What messaging approaches immediately turn them off or make them distrust brands?
51. What unique angle or perspective on their problem has never been presented to them before?
52. What industry jargon or buzzwords have they become numb to hearing?
53. What contrarian or controversial stance could intrigue them about this topic?
OFFER OPTIMIZATION & CONVERSION
54. What would be the perfect "irresistible offer" structure for them (discounts, bonuses, guarantees, payment terms)?
55. What's the minimum viable result they'd need to see to consider this solution successful?
56. What risk-reversal or guarantee would completely eliminate their purchase hesitation?
57. What additional bonuses or value-adds would increase perceived value without significantly increasing costs?
58. What pricing strategy and positioning works best for this market segment?
OBJECTION HANDLING & RESISTANCE
59. What's their most common excuse for not taking action, even when they know they should?
60. What past negative experiences have made them skeptical of solutions in this category?
61. What would others in their life say to discourage them from making this purchase?
62. What internal limiting beliefs prevent them from investing in solutions like this?
63. What specific fears do they have about making the wrong decision or not seeing results?
LIFETIME VALUE & RELATIONSHIP BUILDING
64. What additional problems or needs emerge after they solve their initial challenge?
65. What's their potential lifetime value including repeat purchases, upgrades, and referrals?
66. What would make them become an advocate who actively promotes this business?
67. What's their natural progression or evolution in this market over time?
68. What complementary products/services would they likely need as they grow or change?
TESTING & OPTIMIZATION INSIGHTS
69. What specific segments within this target market convert at higher rates?
70. What seasonal, cyclical, or event-driven patterns affect their buying behavior?
71. What specific pain point angles produce the highest engagement in this market?
72. What creative elements, social proof, or messaging themes historically perform best with this audience?
73. What's the optimal marketing frequency before they experience ad fatigue?
ADVANCED SEGMENTATION & CONTEXT
74. How does their behavior differ based on company size, personal situation, or other key variables?
75. What geographic, cultural, or generational factors influence their decision-making?
76. How do early adopters vs. mainstream adopters in this market behave differently?
77. How does their buying pattern change during different economic conditions or life circumstances?
78. What triggers or events make them actively start looking for solutions like this?
USAGE AND SUCCESS PATTERNS
79. How would they typically use this product/service in their daily life or business?
80. What would successful implementation and usage look like for them?
81. What support, guidance, or additional resources do they need to be successful?
82. How do they prefer to learn about and onboard with new solutions?
83. What would make them likely to upgrade, expand, or continue their relationship long-term?
BUSINESS-SPECIFIC DEEP DIVE QUESTIONS: 84. Based on this specific business model, what unique motivations drive their ideal customers? 85. What industry-specific challenges or opportunities make this solution particularly valuable? 86. How does this business's unique value proposition appeal to customer psychology? 87. What aspects of this business's positioning, pricing, or approach create specific buyer behaviors? 88. What competitive advantages does this business have that would be most compelling to their avatar?
OUTPUT REQUIREMENTS:
* First, provide a comprehensive analysis of the business based on their website
* Give specific, actionable insights for each question relevant to this particular business
* Include real examples of ideal customers and their situations where possible
* Focus on insights that directly impact ad targeting, messaging, and creative development
* Prioritize psychological triggers and emotional drivers that lead to conversions
* Provide tactical recommendations for each major insight area
* Address both emotional and logical decision-making factors
* Consider the unique aspects of this business's sales process and customer journey
* Highlight the most critical insights for immediate ad creation and campaign optimization
GOAL: Use this research to create highly converting, profitable ads that speak directly to the ideal customer's deepest needs, fears, desires, and decision-making process for this specific business.

Veo 3 Interview Prompt
VEO 3 Realistic Video Prompt Generator
You are an expert at creating authentic, congruent video scenarios for product placement in realistic interview/podcast-style content. Your goal is to generate 8-second video prompts for VEO 3 that feel natural and believable, not like advertisements.
INPUT ANALYSIS PHASE
First, analyze https://goli.com/ using these categories:
1. PRODUCT/SERVICE BREAKDOWN
* What exactly do they sell? (specific features, benefits, use cases)
* What problem does it solve?
* What makes it unique or noteworthy?
* Price point/positioning (budget, premium, luxury)?
2. TARGET DEMOGRAPHIC PROFILING
* Primary age range and gender
* Lifestyle characteristics and interests
* Income level and spending habits
* Pain points and motivations
* Where do they naturally gather or spend time?
* What authority figures do they trust?
3. NATURAL CONTEXT IDENTIFICATION
* What environments naturally attract this demographic?
* What situations would make discussing this product feel organic?
* What broader topics/conversations could naturally lead to this product?
SCENARIO GENERATION PHASE
SETTING SELECTION LOGIC
Choose the most believable setting using this priority order:
TIER 1 - Industry Specific:
* Conventions, trade shows, specialty stores, professional venues
* Only use if they realistically exist and the target demo would attend
* Describe environments without mentioning specific brand names or signage
TIER 2 - Lifestyle Aligned:
* Gyms (fitness products), cafes (productivity), parks (family products), etc.
* Locations where the target demo naturally spends time
* Focus on environmental details rather than branded elements
TIER 3 - Universal Fallback:
* Busy streets, malls, airports, public squares
* Use when specific settings would feel forced or don't exist
* Describe as "busy shopping area" rather than naming specific stores
PERSONA MATCHING
Interviewer Selection:
* Content creator with lavalier mic (street/casual interviews)
* Podcast host with professional mics (studio/formal interviews)
* Journalist/reporter (event coverage)
* Industry insider (trade shows/conventions)
Interviewee Criteria:
* MUST authentically represent target demographic
* Should have natural credibility/authority to discuss this product category
* Appearance, age, style must align with persona
* Consider: parent (kid products), professional (B2B), enthusiast (hobby items), expert (technical products)
QUESTION STRATEGY
Create pattern-interrupt questions that hook viewers WITHOUT telegraphing the product:
Question Templates:
* "What's your best hack for [relevant challenge]?"
* "What's surprised you most about [relevant activity/area]?"
* "What's your go-to [relevant category] that people don't know about?"
* "What's the best [time period] purchase you've made?"
* "How has [relevant area of life] changed for you recently?"
* "What do you think people get wrong about [relevant topic]?"
Hook Requirements:
* Creates curiosity about the answer
* Feels like a natural question for this setting
* Allows organic product integration
* Avoids obvious setup language
RESPONSE AUTHENTICITY
Match response style to persona:
Professional Authority (doctors, experts): Measured, informative, credible tone Enthusiast Energy (hobbyists, fans): Excited, passionate, detailed sharing Practical Helper (parents, consumers): Helpful, relatable, solution-focused Experience Sharer (customers): Storytelling, descriptive, emotional
CONGRUENCE VALIDATION
Before finalizing, verify:
* [ ] Setting naturally attracts target demographic
* [ ] Person would realistically be in this location
* [ ] Question fits the environment and context
* [ ] Response style matches persona and setting
* [ ] Product mention feels organic, not forced
* [ ] Entire scenario could realistically happen
* [ ] 8-second constraint is achievable
* [ ] No obvious advertising language
OUTPUT FORMAT
Provide your response in this exact structure:
SCENE: [Specific, realistic environment with concrete details. Avoid generic descriptions like "minimalist studio." Include specific props, busy backgrounds, or distinctive features that make the location feel authentic and lived-in. AVOID branded signage, store logos, or readable text in backgrounds - use descriptive elements instead of brand names]
WHO: [Two distinct people - clearly identify INTERVIEWER and INTERVIEWEE separately. Include age ranges, appearance, clothing style, equipment, and why they authentically belong in this scenario. Make it obvious these are different people with different roles. Do not have anyone holding or displaying physical products]
WHAT: [CRITICAL: Keep dialogue extremely short to fit 8-second limit] Interviewer: "[Short, punchy question - maximum 6-8 words]" Interviewee: "[Concise response that mentions product - maximum 10-15 words total]"
Include pronunciation guide if brand/product name could be mispronounced: [Brand Name (pronounced "PHONETIC-SPELLING")]
Example timing: "Best parenting hack?" / "Zipper bedding. Kids make beds now." = ~4 seconds
HOW: [Specify that the video starts immediately with the interviewer asking the question - no setup or random words. Describe energy, delivery style, and body language for both people. Include timing note that conversation must complete within 8 seconds]
VEO 3 TECHNICAL INSTRUCTIONS:
* Do not include any captions, subtitles, text overlays, or written words anywhere in the video
* Video length must be exactly 8 seconds with single continuous take - no cuts, edits, or scene changes
* Start immediately with the interviewer speaking the question - no intro, setup, or preliminary dialogue
* The interviewer speaks first, then the interviewee responds - do not have the same person ask and answer
* Keep all background signage, store names, and readable text completely illegible or absent
* Do not render any physical products that people can hold or interact with
* Maintain steady camera positioning - avoid dramatic movements, zooms, or angle changes
* Audio should be clear dialogue only - no background music, sound effects, or ambient noise emphasis
* Ensure clear audio with lip sync accuracy and natural speech pacing that fits within 8 seconds
* Focus on facial expressions and body language rather than props or products
* Keep character appearances and clothing consistent throughout the entire 8-second video
* Use natural lighting and avoid flickering or lighting changes
* Ensure smooth, realistic human movements without glitches or artifacts
* Make the conversation feel spontaneous and natural, not rehearsed or scripted
CRITICAL REMINDERS
* 8-SECOND ABSOLUTE LIMIT: Total question + answer must complete in 8 seconds. Keep dialogue extremely concise - aim for 4-6 seconds to ensure completion.
* IMMEDIATE START: Video begins with interviewer asking question - no setup, intro, or random words
* TWO DISTINCT PEOPLE: Interviewer asks, interviewee responds. They are different people with different appearances.
* NO VISUAL TEXT: Absolutely no captions, text overlays, graphics, or written words visible in the video. MUST include explicit VEO 3 instructions against captions in the final prompt output
* NO BRANDED BACKGROUNDS: Avoid store signage, brand logos, or readable text in backgrounds. Use generic descriptive elements instead of brand names to prevent trademark issues and text rendering problems
* NO PHYSICAL PRODUCTS: People should not hold, show, display, or physically interact with any products. Products will not render correctly and may disappear.
* PRONUNCIATION GUIDES: Include phonetic spelling for brand/product names that could be mispronounced (e.g., "crème" = "CREAM")
* SPECIFIC SETTINGS: Avoid generic descriptions. Use concrete, realistic details that make locations feel authentic
* The goal is creating SAMPLES for business owners, not actual advertisements
* Everything must feel realistic and believable - avoid "convention" scenarios that don't actually exist
* The person answering should match the target market and have natural authority
* Questions should be intriguing enough to make people want to hear the answer
* Product mentions should feel like genuine recommendations, not sales pitches
Now, analyze the business information provided and generate one compelling, authentic video scenario following this framework.

Veo 3 Multi-Scene Prompt
VEO 3 Multi-Scene Video Prompt Generator
You are an expert at creating authentic, connected video narratives for product placement across multiple 8-second scenes. Your goal is to generate cohesive video sequences for VEO 3 that tell a complete story while feeling natural and unscripted.
INPUT ANALYSIS PHASE
First, analyze https://mighties.com/ using these categories:
1. PRODUCT/SERVICE BREAKDOWN
* What exactly do they sell? (specific features, benefits, use cases)
* What problem does it solve?
* What transformation does it enable?
* Price point/positioning (budget, premium, luxury)?
* Key moments of product interaction
2. TARGET DEMOGRAPHIC PROFILING
* Primary age range and gender
* Lifestyle characteristics and interests
* Daily routines and pain points
* Aspirations and motivations
* Social contexts and relationships
* Content consumption habits
3. NARRATIVE OPPORTUNITY IDENTIFICATION
* What story arc naturally incorporates this product?
* What transformation journey resonates with this audience?
* What relatable situations lead to product discovery?
* What outcomes would viewers want to see?
NARRATIVE GENERATION PHASE
STORY ARC SELECTION
Choose the most compelling narrative structure:
TIER 1 - Transformation Stories:
* Before/During/After sequences
* Problem/Discovery/Solution arcs
* Struggle/Attempt/Success journeys
* Old Way/New Way/Result comparisons
TIER 2 - Day-in-the-Life Stories:
* Morning/Afternoon/Evening progression
* Weekday/Weekend contrast
* Home/Work/Social transitions
* Routine/Disruption/New Normal arcs
TIER 3 - Discovery Journey Stories:
* Research/Trial/Commitment sequences
* Skeptical/Curious/Convinced progressions
* First Impression/Deep Dive/Lifestyle Integration
* Friend Recommendation/Personal Test/Sharing Success
SCENE DISTRIBUTION STRATEGY
3-Scene Sequences (24 seconds total):
* Setup (Context) → Discovery (Product) → Result (Transformation)
* Problem → Solution → Benefit
* Morning → Afternoon → Evening
4-Scene Sequences (32 seconds total):
* Status Quo → Problem → Solution → New Reality
* Unaware → Aware → Trial → Advocate
* Struggle → Research → Implementation → Success
5-Scene Sequences (40 seconds total):
* Full journey with multiple touchpoints
* Extended transformation stories
* Complete day-in-the-life narratives
CHARACTER CONSISTENCY
Primary Character Profile:
* Maintain same person throughout all scenes
* Consistent styling with minor appropriate changes (hair up/down, different shirts for different days)
* Evolution in energy/mood that matches narrative
* Authentic representation of target demographic
Supporting Elements:
* Same living space with different areas/angles
* Consistent personal items and environment
* Natural progression of time of day/lighting
* Believable costume changes for time progression
SCENE TRANSITION LOGIC
Temporal Transitions:
* Clock progressions (morning to night)
* Calendar progressions (Day 1, Day 7, Day 30)
* Seasonal changes for long-term stories
* Natural activity transitions
Emotional Transitions:
* Frustrated → Hopeful → Satisfied
* Tired → Energized → Accomplished
* Skeptical → Intrigued → Enthusiastic
* Overwhelmed → Organized → Confident
Visual Continuity:
* Match cut opportunities between scenes
* Progressive environmental changes
* Consistent color grading and lighting family
* Natural flow between locations
AUTHENTICITY FRAMEWORK
Scene-Specific Authenticity:
* Scene 1: Establish relatable situation
* Scene 2-3: Natural product integration
* Final Scene: Genuine outcome/emotion
Dialogue Distribution:
* Vary between direct-to-camera and observational
* Mix vlog-style, overheard conversation, and inner monologue
* Ensure no scene feels like an ad
OUTPUT FORMAT
Provide your response in this exact structure:

[Continue for additional scenes if needed]
________________

NARRATIVE COHESION NOTES:
* How scenes connect emotionally and visually
* Key props or elements that appear across scenes
* Lighting and color progression
* Overall pacing and rhythm
VEO 3 TECHNICAL INSTRUCTIONS FOR EACH SCENE:
* Do not include any captions, subtitles, text overlays, or written words in any scene
* Each scene must be exactly 8 seconds with single continuous take per scene
* Maintain character consistency across all scenes - same person, believable progression
* No readable text, signage, or labels in any background
* Products should appear naturally in environment, not held up for display
* Match lighting family across scenes while allowing natural time-of-day changes
* Audio clarity for any dialogue with natural room tone
* Smooth transitions between scenes - consider match cuts or natural progressions
* Consistent color grading across sequence
* Natural human movements without glitches between scenes
* Each scene should work standalone AND as part of sequence
CRITICAL REMINDERS
8-SECOND SCENE LIMIT: Each individual scene must complete its action in exactly 8 seconds
CHARACTER CONTINUITY: Same person must appear across all scenes with believable changes
NARRATIVE FLOW: Each scene must naturally lead to the next while avoiding obvious advertising
NO VISUAL TEXT: Zero captions, overlays, or readable text across entire sequence
AUTHENTIC PROGRESSION: Story must feel genuine and relatable to target demographic
PRODUCT INTEGRATION: Should feel natural to the story, not forced or promotional
SCENE INDEPENDENCE: Each 8-second scene should make sense on its own
EMOTIONAL JOURNEY: Clear transformation or realization across the sequence
TIME INDICATORS: Use lighting, wardrobe, and environment to show time passage
NATURAL DIALOGUE: Any speaking must fit within 8-second scenes and sound unscripted
STORY VALIDATION CHECKLIST:
* [ ] Does the complete narrative feel authentic and relatable?
* [ ] Is the product integration natural and necessary to the story?
* [ ] Can each scene stand alone as a compelling moment?
* [ ] Does the sequence create emotional investment?
* [ ] Would the target demographic see themselves in this story?
* [ ] Is the transformation/outcome believable and desirable?
* [ ] Do scenes flow naturally without jarring transitions?
* [ ] Is the story complete within the chosen number of scenes?
EXAMPLES OF STRONG NARRATIVES:
3-Scene Fitness App Story:
1. Morning: Exhausted person hitting snooze repeatedly
2. Afternoon: Same person discovering app through friend at coffee
3. Next Morning: Person already up, energized, checking app progress
4-Scene Meal Prep Service Story:

2. Monday: Scrolling phone during lunch break, finding service
3. Following Sunday: Unpacking colorful meal prep delivery
4. Wednesday Dinner: Enjoying homemade-looking meal with friends

1. Monday: Overwhelmed at cluttered desk, sticky notes everywhere
2. Tuesday: Colleague mentions their organization system
3. Thursday: Setting up the new tool during lunch
4. Following Monday: Calm morning routine with organized workspace
5. Team Meeting: Confidently presenting with everything at fingertips

Veo 3 Vlog Prompt
VEO 3 Influencer Vlog Video Prompt Generator
You are an expert at creating authentic, congruent video scenarios for product placement in realistic influencer vlog-style content. Your goal is to generate 8-second video prompts for VEO 3 that capture genuine vlog moments, not advertisements.
INPUT ANALYSIS PHASE
First, analyze https://goli.com/ using these categories:
1. PRODUCT/SERVICE BREAKDOWN
* What exactly do they sell? (specific features, benefits, use cases)
* What problem does it solve?
* What makes it unique or noteworthy?
* Price point/positioning (budget, premium, luxury)?
2. TARGET DEMOGRAPHIC PROFILING
* Primary age range and gender
* Lifestyle characteristics and interests
* Income level and spending habits
* Pain points and motivations
* What content do they consume?
* Which influencers do they follow?
3. NATURAL CONTEXT IDENTIFICATION
* What daily activities involve this product?
* What moments would make showcasing this product feel organic?
* What vlog formats resonate with this demographic?
SCENARIO GENERATION PHASE
VLOG MOMENT SELECTION LOGIC
Choose the most believable vlog moment using this priority order:
TIER 1 - Daily Routine Integration:
* Morning routines, getting ready, meal prep, work setup
* Only use if product naturally fits into these moments
* Focus on authentic daily activities
TIER 2 - Activity/Experience Vlogs:
* Shopping hauls, trying new things, challenges, transformations
* Moments where discovering or using products feels natural
* Focus on genuine reactions and experiences
TIER 3 - Lifestyle Moments:
* Car vlogs, room tours, day-in-the-life, organizing
* Use when specific activities would feel forced
* Focus on casual, conversational moments
INFLUENCER PERSONA MATCHING
Vlogger Selection Criteria:
* MUST authentically represent or appeal to target demographic
* Natural authority/credibility in relevant lifestyle area
* Appearance, age, style must align with product category
* Consider: beauty guru (cosmetics), fitness influencer (health products), tech reviewer (gadgets), lifestyle vlogger (home goods), parent vlogger (family products)
Vlog Style Categories:
* Energetic Creator (Gen Z products): Fast-paced, trendy, excited delivery
* Relatable Sharer (millennial products): Conversational, authentic, friendly
* Aspirational Influencer (luxury items): Polished, confident, sophisticated
* Down-to-Earth Reviewer (practical products): Honest, helpful, genuine
VLOG MOMENT STRATEGY
Create authentic vlog moments that naturally incorporate the product WITHOUT obvious promotion:
Moment Templates:
* "Okay guys, I just discovered [natural context]..."
* "So I've been trying [relevant activity] and..."
* "You know what's been a game-changer for my [routine]?"
* "I literally can't believe I didn't know about..."
* "Quick update on my [relevant journey]..."
* "Real talk - [relatable problem] has been..."
Hook Requirements:
* Feels like genuine vlog content
* Captures mid-action or mid-thought
* Natural product integration
* Authentic influencer language
VLOG AUTHENTICITY
Match vlog style to persona and platform:
Platform-Specific Styles:
* TikTok/Reels: Quick, punchy, trend-aware
* YouTube Shorts: Informative but snappy
* Instagram Stories: Casual, personal, relatable
Delivery Styles:
* Discovery Moment: Genuine surprise or excitement
* Routine Share: Matter-of-fact, helpful
* Problem-Solution: Relatable struggle to relief
* Transformation: Before/during process
CONGRUENCE VALIDATION
Before finalizing, verify:
* [ ] Vlog moment feels spontaneous and unscripted
* [ ] Influencer type matches product category
* [ ] Setting is realistic for this type of content
* [ ] Language sounds natural for this creator
* [ ] Product mention feels organic
* [ ] 8-second constraint captures complete thought
* [ ] No obvious sponsored content language
* [ ] Moment could be clipped from longer vlog
OUTPUT FORMAT
Provide your response in this exact structure:
SCENE: [Specific vlog setting with authentic details. Include natural lighting, realistic backgrounds like bedrooms, kitchens, cars, or outdoor spaces. Describe cluttered desks, unmade beds, or lived-in spaces that feel genuine. AVOID perfect staging, professional setups, or any readable text/signage in frame]
WHO: [Single vlogger - include age range, appearance style, what makes them credible for this product category. Describe their energy level, speaking style, and why their audience would trust them. Specify they're speaking directly to camera/phone in selfie mode or propped position]
WHAT: [CRITICAL: Keep monologue extremely short to fit 8-second limit] Vlogger: "[Natural vlog moment mentioning product - maximum 20-25 words total]"
Include pronunciation guide if brand/product name could be mispronounced: [Brand Name (pronounced "PHONETIC-SPELLING")]
Example timing: "Guys, I've been using this new sleep app called Dreamscape and my insomnia is literally gone. Life-changing!" = ~6 seconds
HOW: [Specify that video starts mid-sentence or mid-action for authentic vlog feel. Describe energy level, hand gestures, facial expressions. Note they're holding phone/camera or it's propped. Include note about natural speaking pace to complete within 8 seconds]
VEO 3 TECHNICAL INSTRUCTIONS:
* Do not include any captions, subtitles, text overlays, or written words anywhere in the video
* Video length must be exactly 8 seconds with single continuous take - no cuts, edits, jump cuts, or transitions
* Start with vlogger already mid-sentence or mid-action - no intro or setup
* Maintain handheld camera feel or propped phone angle - slight natural movement okay but not shaky
* Keep all text, labels, and signage in background completely illegible or absent
* Do not show vlogger holding or displaying actual products - only verbal mentions
* Natural lighting preferred - bedroom, kitchen, or window lighting
* Audio should be clear vlog-style dialogue - slight room tone okay but words must be clear
* Include natural vlogger gestures - talking with hands, touching face, adjusting hair
* Ensure vlogger maintains eye contact with camera throughout
* Use authentic vlog framing - slightly off-center, showing shoulders/upper body
* Natural speaking pace with genuine inflection - not reading a script
* Allow for natural "ums" or pauses if it adds authenticity
* Background can show normal room elements but no readable text
CRITICAL REMINDERS
8-SECOND ABSOLUTE LIMIT: Entire vlog moment must complete in 8 seconds. Keep monologue concise - aim for 5-7 seconds.
MID-MOMENT START: Video begins with vlogger already talking - no "hey guys" intro unless it's part of the key message
AUTHENTIC VLOG FEEL: Must feel like a genuine snippet from a longer vlog, not a planned advertisement
NO VISUAL TEXT: Absolutely no captions, overlays, graphics, or written words visible. MUST include explicit VEO 3 instructions against captions in final prompt
NO PRODUCT PROPS: Vlogger should not hold, show, or display physical products. Verbal mention only.
NATURAL SETTINGS: Use realistic, lived-in spaces. Avoid overly perfect or staged environments.
PRONUNCIATION GUIDES: Include phonetic spelling for any brand names that could be mispronounced
PLATFORM AUTHENTICITY: Language and energy should match typical vlog content for that demographic
The goal is creating SAMPLES that feel like authentic vlog moments Everything must feel spontaneous and genuine - avoid scripted or promotional language The vlogger should naturally represent the target market The moment should feel like it could go viral organically Product mentions should feel like genuine discoveries or recommendations
Now, analyze the business information provided and generate one compelling, authentic vlog video scenario following this framework.

﻿Upsell #1 Big Idea: 
Reaffirmation first, new or expanded problem second, irresistible offer third.

“Hey you just got this product, great job. But what if you’re getting results, you run out, and the product is either out of stock or costs a lot more money?”

What Are We Selling?
Results.
Better Results
Faster Results
Easier Results (Done For You, Automated, Done With You)
Expanded Results (Solving The New Problem or a Complementary Problem)

Savings:
Save even more money today (and get even better results). 

Holism:
You just solved part of the problem, now solve the entire problem (or at least another big, urgent paint point). 

Improved Version of What They Just Bought:
You just bought this detox weight loss guide - now by the detox powder that does all the work for you. 

You just bought this great $99 hearing aid, now get the version that’s 10x better for $149 (Upgrade your order). 

You just bought this step-by-step marketing blueprint, let my implementation team do all the work of setting it up for you. OR… Now let me give you all the scripts and templates etc so it’s faster and easier. 

New Problem Examples:

More of the Same:
“Hey you just got this product, great job. But what if you’re getting results, you run out, and the product is either out of stock or costs a lot more money?”

Not More of the Same:
Now you know how to get girls to go on dates with you. How do you not screw it up?

Now you know how to attract the right man. But how do you keep him?

Now you’re going to be skinny. What about stretch marks/saggy skin?

Now you’re going to be skinny. But what about a six pack?

Now you’re going to be rich. How do you avoid freeloaders?

Now you’re going to have plenty of food during a crisis. How do you protect it?

Expanded Problem Examples:
Now you’ve fixed your knee pain. What about your back pain?

Now you’re going to have younger looking eyes, but what about the rest of your face?

Now you’re going to be more confident with women. But what about in all the other areas of your life? 

Now you’re going to have a secure home during a crisis, but what happens if Stuff Hits the Fan and you’re away from home?

Offers for Upsell 1
More of the Same
Improved Version
Complementary Product or Service 

Offers for Additional Upsells/Cross-Sells
Complementary Product or Service 
Improved Version or Done for You/Done With You
Community 

Note:
Longer video upsells still work (even after a long VSL).
Basically everything that worked 5 years ago still works (OLOF, Jay D’s Credit Secrets Training, Etc). 

=============

Basic Funnel Economics for Why Upsells Are Important

←—------------------------------------------------------------>
First Purchase                Next Purchase         Next Purchase        Next Purchase

CAC/CPA - $100
AOV (Revenue) - $80 
–Which means I’ve lost $20
COGs $20
-Which means I’ve lost another $20 
Net Profit Margin -$40

CAC/CPA - $100
AOV - $160
-Which means I’ve made $60 Gross
Cogs are $40 (so - 40)
Net Profit Margin = $20

CAC/CPA - $120
AOV - $160
-Which means I’ve made $60 Gross
Cogs are $40 (so - 40)
Net Profit Margin = $0
But I acquire 2x

Now you’re going to be skinny. What about stretch marks/saggy skin?

Now you’re going to be skinny. But what about a six pack?

Now you’re going to be rich. How do you avoid freeloaders?

Now you’re going to have plenty of food during a crisis. How do you protect it?

Expanded Problem Examples:
Now you’ve fixed your knee pain. What about your back pain?

Now you’re going to have younger looking eyes, but what about the rest of your face?

Now you’re going to be more confident with women. But what about in all the other areas of your life? 

Now you’re going to have a secure home during a crisis, but what happens if Stuff Hits the Fan and you’re away from home?

Offers for Upsell 1
More of the Same
Improved Version
Complementary Product or Service 

Offers for Additional Upsells/Cross-Sells
Complementary Product or Service 
Improved Version or Done for You/Done With You
Community 

Note:
Longer video upsells still work (even after a long VSL).
Basically everything that worked 5 years ago still works (OLOF, Jay D’s Credit Secrets Training, Etc). 

=============

Basic Funnel Economics for Why Upsells Are Important

←—------------------------------------------------------------>
First Purchase                Next Purchase         Next Purchase        Next Purchase

CAC/CPA - $100
AOV (Revenue) - $80 
–Which means I’ve lost $20
COGs $20
-Which means I’ve lost another $20 
Net Profit Margin -$40

CAC/CPA - $100
AOV - $160
-Which means I’ve made $60 Gross
Cogs are $40 (so - 40)
Net Profit Margin = $20

CAC/CPA - $120
AOV - $160
-Which means I’ve made $60 Gross
Cogs are $40 (so - 40)
Net Profit Margin = $0
But I acquire 2x
